— Rabbi Howard Greenstein
David Gaffney begins his day at the morning minyan. He puts on his tefillin.
At the appropriate times in the service he leads the mourners kaddish. When it’s
time to take the Torah from the ark, and it’s placed on the reading table, he takes
over the reading of the Torah portion for that day. At the conclusion of the
reading, he recites a mi sheberach for the sick members of the congregation. He
follows that with the El Moleh Rachamim to honor the memory of one whose
yarzeit is observed that day. At the end of the service, he delivers an always
interesting D’var Torah. He then goes to his office, where he gets ready for his
appointment with someone who is preparing for conversion.
“Thank you Rabbi Gaffney for making me feel at home when l first met
you 12 years ago, when 1 was Catholic and feeling very foreign in the synagogue.
Thank you for helping me be certain I had a part in Leah’s naming. Thank you
for the hours of training you gave me- Beginner’s Judaism (twice), and my
conversion to Judaism. You helped me to know that I am “just as Jewish ” even
though 1 was not born a Jew. I was nervous, you were uplifting. ”— Karen Dubin
It’s still Monday
Rabbi Gaffney takes time to speak with a congregant who has dropped by
to inquire about a private matter. Then he has a appointment to counsel a troubled
couple about their marriage, and, if necessary, explain the criteria for a Jewish
divorce. On a happier note, he has a meeting with proud parents to talk to them
about the brit of their new son.
“Here is a picture of you presiding over the brit of our grandson, Martin
Arthur Cohen, on June 26, 1997. You spoke of the wonderful, special baby in our
lives and how fortunate the baby was that his great grand-father, Harry Haber,
age 97, could be there. We remember that with such fondness”
— Helen Haber Siegel
The day is still not over. Rabbi hurries home in time for a little dinner, then
it’s back to the Center for a Religious Committee meeting, and finally home for
what’s left of the evening.
Now it’s Tuesday
The day begins quietly enough. All he has to do is, visit the hospitals to
comfort the sick. Then it’s back to the Center to prepare for the Adult Bar/Bat
Mitzvah Class which will meet that evening.
“/ want you to know that becoming a Bat Mitzvah is perhaps the most
gratifying thing I’ve ever done for myself. I have learned so much about being
Jewish and living a Jewish life. My eyes have been opened to so many daily
miracles that I previously took for granted. I have learned that Torah, laws and
tradition provide a wonderful ‘support system’ to guide us through times. Now I
have the tools to begin to learn more and to enjoy being Jewish. I thank you for
teaching me, taking me seriously and being my friend.— Elyse Whitman
He takes time to stop by the Solomon Schechter School to talk with the
children, and tell them Bible stories. Mr. Kennedy and the Rabbi discusses plans
for the songfest for the second day of Sukkot. Soon, it’s time to lead services at

join the club!
Through the Jacksonville Jewish Center’s merchandise scrip
program, the V.I.P. Club, VESTED INTEREST PURCHASING,
a portion of what you spend is given to the Center by the popular
merchants listed below. You simply order merchandise certificates
directly from the Center for each business you plan to patronize and
spend them as you would any other certificate. So every time you
shop, you contribute to the Center without spending any more money!
Great for all your regular shopping and gift giving, too. Imagine
buying cash certificates to so many different stores all in one place!
What a time saver.
The V.I.P. Club is one fundraising program in which everyone in
the congregation can participate. It allows the synagogue to benefit
without any change in your spending habits or in the places you
shop.
Monday is V.I.P. Day! You may place an order any, or every.
Monday by 2 p.m. at the Jacksonville Jewish Center (no phone
orders).Your order will be ready for you to pick up at the Center on
the immediate Friday.
Shop at Albertson’s with your free COMMUNITY
PARTNERS CARD. You can help the Center every time
you buy groceries at Albertson’s. Simply present your
Community Partner Card to the cashier any time during
check-out. Your card will be scanned and the Center will
automatically receive a refund of a portion of your purchase.
It’s that easy! Get your card at the Center office.

Lifecycle Events
Burial and Mourning
Center Cemetery
The Center owns and operates two cemeteries, both adjacent
to the Evergreen Cemetery in North Jacksonville. Both are beautiful
pieces of property with large shade trees and mature landscaping.
The original cemetery is referred to as the “Old Cemetery.” The
newer cemetery is known as the “Center Memorial Park.” A new section
has been opened. The Center
provides complete maintenance
of these grounds. Both
cemeteries are open daylight
hours every day except
Shabbat and Jewish holidays.
A Memorial Service is
conducted each year on the Sunday between Rosh Hashanah and Yom
Kippur at each of the cemeteries. To reach the Old Cemetery, travel
north on North Main Street to Winona. Make a right on Winona and go
until you reach Gate 5. The Old Cemetery is on the left. To reach the
Center Memorial Park, travel north on North Main Street to 43rd Street,
which is beyond Winona. Make a right on 43rd Street and the entrance is
on the next right, which is Liberty Street.
Just as with other life cycle events at the Center, burial and mourning
rites are reserved for Center members. Therefore, only full members may
purchase a plot in one of the Center cemeteries. For more information
regarding the purchase of cemetery plots, please call the Center
administrative office.
We thank the voulnteers

There is a Jewish way of life and there is a Jewish way of death.
The Jacksonville Hevra Kaddisha, an independent organization
serving the entire Jewish community, is dedicated to preparing the deceased
with dignity and respect in accordance with Jewish tradition. Families
can be assured that our membership is made up of the most dedicated and
sincere individuals in our community. Our members need no recognition,
only the satisfaction of performing a mitzvah that requires no “thank-
you.”
The Hevra Kaddisha is self supporting, and has grown in strength
through the years making it possible to serve the Jewish community and
individuals regardless of their financial means. We serve 24 hours a day,
and can be of service and comfort to any family by contacting any of our
officers.
The respect, love and consideration that is afforded individuals while
living, must also be given to the deceased.
- Nathan Sandler, President

Maintenance & Housekeeping Staff
The maintenance and housekeeping staff work diligently to keep our building
clean and presentable at all times. Richard Ford, our Maintenance Supervisor, takes
pride in his staff, and devotes much of his time to taking care of all the physical
needs required by the many events which take place throughout the year. Volunteers
appreciate the special attention they receive from the maintenance department.

A Message from Rabbi Gaffney
71" 2
September 1998
Elul 5758
Dear Friends,
Our tradition suggests that the
most authentic form of prayer is an
expression of gratitude. Jewish
children are taught to begin each day
with the words - “Modeh ani Vfa-
nech ...” -“I am grateful to you, O
God...” At the end of each meal we
recite the words “Nodeh Vcha...” -
“We thank you, O God”. At the
conclusion of the day the evening
services urges us to say -“Modim
anachnu ...” -“We thank you O
God.” On Shabbat and holidays the
92nd Psalm is recited -“Tov I’hodot
Vcha ...” - “It is good to give thanks
to You, O God.”
As I consider these past 25
years (...it is hard to believe ...a
quarter of a century??) with our
Jewish Center family, I find this
tradition of thankfulness to be the
most accurate reflection of my
sentiments. The words on this page
come in the form of a -“hakarat ha-
tov... ” -a recognition of the goodness
and blessing which is mine in the
association that I have enjoyed with
so many friends for so many years.
I am grateful that I am blessed
with a congregational family that is
second to none in its warmth and
devotion. From time to time, when
rabbis “let their hair down” at a
convention or meeting, there are the
inevitable complaints by colleagues
who describe their struggle with their
congregational board ...or their
membership. I find myself thinking
that I have no frame of reference to
understand their dilemmas. From the
very first day that Inge and I came to
Jacksonville, we were touched by the
warmth and pleasantness, the
sweetness and sensitivity of the
members of this congregation. We
Rabbi David and Inge Gaffney
have stood in awe in recognition of
the sacrifices of time, effort and
substance that so many have made
and continue to make on behalf of
our beloved Center. We are proud
to have been part of this grand
spiritual adventure which the Jewish
Center has experienced and which it
will be celebrating at its centennial,
in just a few years. I am blessed in
that so many of you have permitted
me to enter the inner sanctuary of
your hearts and souls. It is no small
achievement that over twenty-five
years a tapestry has been woven
with threads that link our lives in joy
and sorrow, in hopes and dreams.
The term rabbi is a term which
signifies relationship. As the word
“father” implies a child ...as the word
“husband” implies a wife ...the term
“rabbi” means teacher. In a rabbinic
text, The Ethics of the Fathers, one
rabbi confessed ... “I have learned
much from my teachers; but from my
students I have learned most of all.”
A rabbi learns most from those he
attempts to teach. I have learned so
much from you. I have learned about
the innocence of faith from the
children of our schools and have
thrilled in their excitement as they
grow in knowledge of Jewish life. I
have learned about the wonder and
mystery of love from couples before
whom I stand under the huppah\ and
have been moved by the idealism of
our young people as their youth
groups engage in a variety of activities
of Tikkun Olam. I continue to be
inspired by the depths of commitment
of the lay leaders of our congregation
and am heartened by expressions of
Jewish responsibility from those who
labor unceasingly for the community,
for Israel and for the Jewish people.
I have learned courage from those
who have lived with the burden of
sorrow and illness and the meaning
of joy from those who have been
touched by life’s blessings. I have
felt the warmth from so many of you
who attend Shabbat services ...and
devotion from those who attend our
daily minyan. Most of all I have
learned about friendship from each
of you who have offered your heart
in warmth and love to Inge and me.
Friends, as we mark this
personal milestone I am reminded of
the teaching of Rabbi Tarphon who
stated -“hayom ketzer v’hamlacha
m’rubah”... “the day is short and
there is so much work to be done.”
Whatever the personal achievements
and aspirations for our beloved
congregation, I recognize that it would
not have been possible without the
support, cooperation and effort of an
extraordinary professional staff. In
some cases these relationships
extend over a long period of time
...Rabbi Dov Kentof, Mr. Willard
Kennedy, Marilyn Sandler and Ted
Gross have shared a substantial
portion of their life, professionally,
with our congregation. In other cases
relationships are more recent but no
less valuable ...Cantor Aron Heller,
Bruce Horovitz, Shirley Bielski and
Dale Schemer. It has also been most
rewarding to be able to share each
day with numbers of devoted
individuals in our administrative
offices, beginning with my secretary
Dereen Murray and including Kim
Winters, Inez Achord, Elaine Metlin
continued on page 7

Rabbi Kentof’s Message
Every community on Earth, from
the most primitive to the most civilized,
passes its culture on from generation to
generation. Accordingly, the main concern
of each generation is what to make of the
next. In free societies, the concern is that
children reach their full potential as men
and women — that they grow up to do
their part to improve the world, both
materially and spiritually.
At various times, bills of rights
have been written for children, giving
specific expression to this principle.
These children’s bills of rights embody
a major American ideal. They define the rights of all
American children, whatever their faith, race, occupation,
social status, or ethnic origin. However, the children of
the Jewish community have a claim to additional rights,
which only the Jewish communities of the United States
have the obligation to secure. These rights are:
1. A continuing Jewish education that will give them
accurate knowledge and sympathetic understanding of the
life, labors, ideals, struggles, and achievements of the
Jewish people, from the beginning of their history to the
present time. This will give them the opportunity to express
themselves and become part of the continuation and
development of the Jewish religion and heritage.
2. An insight into what being a member of the Jewish
community means for their growth; a feeling that belonging
to the community, participating in its works and ways and
contributing to its culture and ideals, enhances their freedom
as individuals; and understanding of their oneness with fellow
Jews in the United States, Israel, and around the world.
3. An environment, in home, school,
synagogue, center, and association
where they are understood and guided
to full self-realization.
4. An upbringing that will strengthen
his/her commitment to democracy as
the way of life most in accord with
Jewish teaching, the welfare of
America, and the dignity of humanity,
so they will develop a deep sense of
kinship with all people.
5. A democratic community in which
they can develop, through the spiritual
and professional training of the
community’s professionals, to give devoted and effective
service to their community.
We devote the Jacksonville Jewish Center
Supplemental Schools Department to instilling these rights
in our students.
To reach our goals, we employ the best teaching staff
available, giving them new and innovative curriculum ideas
along with textbooks, audio-visual equipment, and much more,
so they can be successful in helping your child to learn and
grow.
But, we do not do it alone. The support and participation
of our parents is crucial to the success of our program.
Parents who take active, supportive roles in their children’s
Hebrew education often see the best results. We look forward
to continuing this partnership in the year ahead.
For myself, Alina, and our children, let me wish you
a Happy and Sweet New Year.
Rabbi Dov Kentof
Director of Education & Youth
9
===== PAGE 18 =====
President’s Message
Shanah Tovah!
As our congregation approaches its
100th anniversary, we have a lot to be
thankful for, and we have a lot to be
proud of.
We are thankful that Evan Yegelwel,
and all other past presidents of the Center,
have done their jobs so well to bring this
congregation and its schools to such
heights of excellence and quality. We are
thankful that you, our members, feel such
warmth and closeness to our synagogue that you openly
volunteer your time and are generous with your
contributions. The tireless energy and devotion dedicated
by the Center’s many volunteers make so many things
possible for all of our membership — from daily minyans
to high holiday preparations, to the day-to-day tasks that
make our synagogue run so well. The continuing generosity
of our members has allowed us to expand and improve
our programs and our ability to serve all Center members.
The recent generous bequest by Mrs. Esther Galinsky will
enhance the Solomon Schechter Day School and the
Center’s educational programs for generations to come.
We are thankful for the good fortune to have such
outstanding professionals at the Center. It is truly
extraordinary to have a Rabbi who has demonstrated such
tremendous commitment and untiring energy to our
congregation. We owe Rabbi Gaffney a tremendous debt
for all that he has given our congregation over the last 25
years. We are also very appreciative for the tremendous
enthusiasm, creative ideas, and genuine warmth Rabbi
Kentof has shared with our congregation over the past 20
years. Dov has excited and motivated our youth for two
decades, for which we are truly blessed. Cantor Heller,
Bruce Horovitz, Willard Kennedy and all
of our professional staff have done a
wonderful job maintaining the Center’s
excellent level of service to our members,
for which we are all beneficiaries.
We as a congregation have much to
be proud of. We are proud of our many
programs for all ages, which keep the
Center open from dawn until well after
dusk. We are proud of our facility and
campgrounds, which have no equal. We
are proud of an outstanding pre-school
program which introduces Judaism and Jewish values to
children at the youngest ages. We are proud of our excellent
Solomon Schechter Day School with learning standards
so high that children graduate from our school with a
superb ability to compete and succeed. We are proud of
our supplemental school and youth programs, instilling
our youth with Jewish education, fellowship, and values.
Most of all, we are both thankful and proud of our
members, without whom we would not be such a vibrant
and active congregation. By your presence, support and
energy, you make the Center a living legacy of Jewish
continuity for us, our children and future generations.
On behalf of the officers, executive committee,
committee chairmen and board, and all those here at the
Center who volunteer and work to make our Center exceed
your expectations, we wish you a very good year.
And on behalf of Beth, Daniel, Rebecca, Jennifer,
and Benjamin, I wish you a healthy, happy, and prosperous
new year!
— Mark J. Shorstein
Mark J. Shorstein
President
Berman Bros., Inc.

Youth Activities
White Water Rafting Experience
Led by Rabbi Dov Kentof
This year’s trip was a tremendous success. The challenges were great; the
river was wild; everyone survived and had a wonderful time. Many thanks to all
the adults for their help, especially Ava Axelrod, who prepared all the meals, and
Rabbi Dov Kentof, without whom there would have been no trip. Here are some
of the comments from the participants:
“A great chance to share the great
outdoors and make new friends.”
“Start as strangers, end as friends. Time
to be with your child away from the
usual distractions. You can do it even if
you think you can’t.”
“Intimate bonding experience.”
“A wonderful opportunity to leave daily
life behind and rediscover what’s really
important.”
“I could see why Rabbi Kentof loves
the kids so — they are intriguingly
unique from one another, yet each one
comes with such gifts. Yes, they are
obvious reflections and extensions of
their parents, but it is easy to see their
own spirits, which need our patience,
nurturing and appreciation. I was so
pleased with the instant companionship,
the supportive teamwork and senses of
humor.”
“It was awesome — I gained 5 lbs.
(thanks, Ava!)”
LTI
Leadership Training Institute
Summer Encampment 1998
Summers are topped off with a
unique experience at Camp Blue Star
for one week during the month of
August. Teenagers from 7th grade and
up are encouraged to take the
opportunity to participate in this
program which includes informal
classes and discussion groups, cultural
activities and special evening activities
in addition to a full range of camp sports
and social activities. The camp provides
two unique programs: Kadima, grade 6,
7 & 8, and USY, grades 9 through 12.
Those attending were: Geri Bernard,
Laney Cohen, Megan Cohen,
Stefanie Epstein, Eli Fleet, Jared
Fleet, Dena Mizrahi, Gal Nevo,
Natalie Osterer, Jeffrey Shenkman,,
Dani Spriggs, Jonathan Spriggs and
Max Talpalar.
Center Youth Banquet
May 17,1998
At the conclusion of the activity
year, the Youth Commission holds a
banquet to honor the officers, advisors
and volunteers from each Center Youth
Group. Newly elected officers for the
coming year are introduced. The lovely
ceremony and program are always
enjoyed by the young people and their
families who attend the banquet.

Community Agencies
River Garden
HEBREW HOME/WOLFSON HEALTH & AGING CENTER
“Honor thy father and mother that thy days may be long...”
It was this commandment which inspired the founding of River Garden
Hebrew Home in 1946. It was this commandment which nourished the love and
care that for more than fifty years has made River Garden a nationally recognized
model of excellence in its field. It was this commandment that made it necessary
to create a Home that is welcoming to families and encourages its use as an
extension of family space. River Garden residents are a part of the community, not
apart from it.
The River Garden Hebrew Home has also become the anchor of a growing
system of elder services. The success of River Garden is based on the tradition of
meeting 100 percent of local Jewish community needs and of serving rich and
poor alike with excellence. The River Garden Foundation accepts donations to
help River Garden continue to meet its mission. This would not be possible
without substantial charitable support from the community and the work of The
River Garden Foundation to stimulate planned gift annuities, trusts and bequests.
River Garden’s programs of short-term rehabilitative/respite care, long¬
term residential care, Alzheimers’ and Adult Day Care, serve over 180 people on
any given day. These programs are guided by a devoted, professional full time
staff of over 200. Staff includes physicians and beauticians; nurses, social workers,
pharmacists, activities specialists; physical occupational and speech therapists;
dieticians, etc. In addition, scores of dedicated volunteers help create a special
caring community.
Located on a 33 acre Mandarin campus containing lush Florida oak and
pine trees, a private lake, meandering walking paths, River Garden is the perfect
setting for residents and visitors. River Garden is a community where people live,
love and care; a community of many lifestyles and of rich Jewish content, and a
community which every day strives to live up to the mandate of the Fifth
Commandment.
In recent years, life on campus has become more active and attractive with
the completion of the Coves, the elegant, affordable retirement community.

An elegant yet affordable
retirement community is located on
River Garden’s beautiful 33 acre campus
in Mandarin. Sponsored by the not-for-
profit River Garden Holding Company,
The Coves offers security, club-house
living and the opportunity for continued
growth during the retirement years in a
Jewishly sponsored environment.
The River Garden Foundation is a philanthropic organization, established to
provide resources for programs and facilities to enhance the quality of life for the
aged. Its primary purpose is to fund the not-for-profit River Garden system of
services.
The foundation is dedicated to helping the elderly remain in control of their
own lives by assuring services to people at all levels of need and financial ability.
The aim of the Foundation is to keep pace with the changing needs of the
aging through programs that meet a broad array of health care needs, as well as
provide a full spectrum of residential options.

Scouting
Boy Scout Troop 14
Troop 14 carried on the scouting tradition at the Jacksonville Jewish Center with another year of outdoor
fun, adventure and activities in 1997-98. Bob Fleet served as Scoutmaster, and was assisted by Assistant
Scoutmasters Louis Schwartz and Billy Wilensky. Youth leadership was provided by Eli Fleet as Junior
Assistant Scoutmaster, Justin Jackrel as Senior Patrol Leader, and Jared Fleet
as Assistant Senior Patrol Leader.
The troop camped out this year at Stephen Foster State Park in the
Okeefenokee Swamp, aboard the USS Yorktown in South Carolina, at
Marineland, and at Fort Wilderness in Walt Disney World. On all campouts
kashrut and Shabbat are observed.
This year’s programs included visiting the new City Hall and attending a
City Council Meeting as part of the requirements for the Citizenship in the
Community Merit Badge, earning the Climbing Merit Badge at Peak Performers
Climbing Gym and working on the Safety Merit Badge with a member of the Northeast Florida Safety Council.
This summer, the scouts attended camp at Camp Powhatan in the Blue Ridge Mountains of Virginia.
They went rafting on the New River in West Virginia and earned many merit badges.
Troop 14 is open to any boy age 11 to 18 who enjoys camping, sports, and other outdoor activities. We
welcome you to come to our meetings at the Center on Thursday nights. The troop also welcomes participation
from adults interested in providing volunteer assistance. For more information call Bob Fleet at 268-2746
(H) or 730-8103 (W).
1998 - 1999 will the 80th year that Troop 14 has provided Jewish youth a Boy Scouting experience. We
look forward to a great 80th year!
Great summer fun at Camp Powhatan.
Aboard the USS Yorktown.

Community Organizations
Hadassah
“Hadassah has always been an important bridge to peace.
By treating all people without regard to nationality or religion—
Hadassah has shown the world what peace in the Middle East
will look like.” -Yitzchak Rabin, Jerusalem, 1994.
Judaism teaches that is not enough to avoid iniquity —
we must actively pursue righteousness and justice at home, in
the, community, and in the world. In this tradition, Hadassah
was founded in 1912 by Henrietta Szold to bring public health
services to pre-state Israel. Today, more than 300,000 American
women support our network of Israel projects in addition to
our volunteer work at home. Across the US, Hadassah promotes
health education, community service, and Jewish education
and research. Hadassah advocates on issues ranging from
Israel-US relations to First Amendment protections to women’s
rights and health concerns.
One by one, we must each take responsibility for
transforming hopes, promises, and echoes into deeds.
Jacksonville Hadassah invites your participation in one of our
four groups: Hannah Senesch, Shir Li, Tikva, and Nurse’s
Gouncil.
For information please contact any of our presidents:
Chapter Phyllis Goldberg and Robin Morris
Hannah Senesch Adele Levitin and Jean Weinberg
Shir Li Robin Allerding
Tikva Leslie Held
Jacksonville Chapter of Hadassah Board:
National Council of Jewish Women
The National Council of Jewish Women (NCJW)-
Jacksonville Section, Inc. is a volunteer organization, inspired
by Jewish values, that works through a program of research,
education, advocacy, and community service to improve the
quality of life for women, children and families, and strives to
ensure individual rights and freedoms for all.
The Jacksonville section was established in 1939, and
has been involved in the following programs:
• Tutoring “at risk” girls at PACE to provide them with a second
chance to earn a diploma and job skills;
• Bringing kosher meals, as well as a caring word, to the
homebound (Kosher Kart);
• Starting a model program, later adopted nationwide, to
provide abused children with a voice in the court system
(Guardian Ad Litem);
• Bringing the Home Instructional Program for Preschool
Youngsters (HIPPY), a school-readiness program for at risk
4 and 5 year olds to Jacksonville;
• Spearheading advocacy efforts at the local, state, and
national levels for programs and policies which impact our
six priority areas, which include women’s issues, children
and youth, health and aging, constitutional rights, Jewish
Life, and Israel;
• Provide educational monthly programs to educate the
community about a variety of topics.
For information, contact Ellen Rubens 737-1552

Cantor Heller’s Message
We are once again at that exciting
period of the year— the High Holiday
Season. It begins with Rosh Hashanah,
the New Year, and ends with Yom
Kippur, the Day of Atonement, more
appropriately called Yom Hadin, the Day
of Judgment.
Rosh Hashanah is also known by
other names — Yom Hazikaron and Yom
Teruah. These names are especially
significant in the cycle of life.
Yom Hazikaron means Day of Remembrance. We
use this day to remember, to reflect and to evaluate the
year gone by. Was it good, bad, or ordinary? Well, for me,
it’s been an extraordinary year of blessing, excitement and
challenge. I have been blessed to finally have my family
join me, and to spend our first Yom Tov together in our
new home, with our new friends. Thankfully, the transition
particularly for my children, Lisa, Jonathan and Daniel,
was made smooth by the unbelievable support of this
wonderful community.
My son Jonathan celebrated his Bar Mitzvah in our
new synagogue this past year, and I was once again given
the opportunity to experience first hand the excitement
that all parents feel when their children assume the
responsibilities of Jewish adults. I knew this would be a
memorable occasion, but the rallying of the entire
community around my family exceeded my expectations.
I thank you all.
There has been, too, the wonderful challenge of
preparing your children to take their places on our bima,
giving special meaning to the expression V dor v’dor, “from
generation to generation.” I was privileged to share the
excitement of the families whose sons and daughters
celebrated their own Bar and Bat Mitzvot, after months of
nervous studying under the watchful eye of the “new
Cantor.” Each celebration reinforced
the fact that Judaism is vibrant in our
community. We are all truly blessed
to have a wonderful reservoir of
children, who are given, through our
Center school programs, the tools by
which to live a good Jewish life. These
special events, each one unique, are a
source of immense inspiration to me.
But more challenges lay ahead.
Yom Teruah, the Day the Shofar is
Sounded, emphasizes this. We blow the shofar for that
very reason — to alert ourselves to the challenges of making
ourselves, and our world, better. The range of these issues
is extensive and diverse, but for me none is more important
than strengthening and deepening our involvement in Jewish
education. The commitment and achievements, of which
our congregation is justifiably proud, are the result of 25
years of dedication and guidance by Rabbi Gaffney,
supported by the effervescent energy of Rabbi Kentof, to
educate our youth and adults. Yet, there is so much more
to do. The tekiah of the shofar will stir me to continue to
strive to fulfill my own goals, and to rise to the challenges
of serving the needs of all sectors of this community. My
focus will be on our children. However, the support of
parents in these endeavors is paramount to our success. I
look forward to their continued active engagement.
With these thoughts, let us face the New Year with
confidence and may Yom Hadin, the Day of Judgment, be
the day that we are sealed in the Book of Life, health and
happiness in order that we may meet the challenges that
lie ahead.
On behalf of Lynette, my family, and myself, I extend
to you L Shanah Tovah Tikatevu.
— Cantor Aron Heller
Cantor Aron Heller
SSDS Youth Choir, under the direction of Cantor
Heller, performed at a Sisterhood Luncheon.
Teaching a new song.
A seminar for Bar/Bat Mitzvah students and
parents lead by Rabbi Kentof and Cantor Heller.

Recreation
Sunday Sports Basketball Program
The Sunday Sports Association (SSA) provides area
youth with alternative athletic programs on Sunday
afternoons. All the games and practices are held in the
Fletcher-Selber Auditorium of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center. This year over 195 children, 40 volunteer coaches
and volunteer referees played hard, developed skills and
practiced sportsmanship. Thank you to Gayle Bailys who
coordinated a very successful program and the volunteer
coaches for their valuable assistance and time. We look
forward to an exciting 1998-99 season.

Special Events
Annual Congregation Meeting and Special Awards
Newly elected president,Mark Shorstein (r)
presented a gift to Evan Yegelwel, as a token of
the congregations gratitude for his efforts as
symnagogue president for the past two years.
The annual congregation meeting gives members a glimpse of
the business conducted monthly by the Center’s officers and board of
directors. With the ceremony befitting the occasion, this meeting began
with an invocation from Rabbi Gaffney, and the singing of Hatikvah
lead by Cantor Heller. President Evan Yegelwel delivered a “state of
the synagogue” message and chairmen of standing committees gave
reports on the accomplishments made throughout the year. In election
years, like this one, the slate of new officer is presented. It was a
festive evening, complete with dessert reception. This year’s meeting
was made even more special by the honors bestowed on four very
deserving people.
Inez Achord

Dedicated Service

With a wealth of
facts in her head, Inez can
give a family history on
any Center member
without blinking an
eyelid. To every member,
she is known for her
accurate record keeping.
To those in need of advice,
she is a trustworthy
confidant. To those in

known for her caring and
understanding. She exhibits
a faithfulness and sense of
responsibility that have
set a unique standard for
others to follow. We wish
her many years of good
health, and mazel tov on a
job well done.
For 21 years, Evelyn
has played the role of
devoted caregiver to
generations of Center
children. Not only has she
efficiently managed the
Solomon Schechter Day
School office for so many
years, but she has mothered,
doctored, nursed, listened,
baby-sat, advised, praised,
reprimanded and affected
not only our children, but
our teachers, leaders and
principals, as well. Evelyn
always rises to the
occasion, unselfishly
giving of her time, energy
and spirit whenever the
situation demands. She’s an
invaluable employee and
friend.
Give her a job and
you can count on Kate to
get it done. We are so
lucky that Kate includes
the Center in her busy
volunteer schedule. With
reliability, charm and
warmth, Kate shows up
weekly to fill in the gaps
of the very busy Center
youth department. Rabbi
Kentof’s “middle arm”, all
Kate demands is an
occasional cup of coffee
and a pile of work to
complete. She can be
counted on to brighten the
day. Kate’s vitality,
dedication and positive
attitude make her
invaluable and much
appreciated.
We claim Naomie
as ours alone, but it is not
surprising to find that
she also gives her time to
Baptist Hospital, Chevra
Kaddisha, the Jacksonville
Symphony, the Duval
County School System,
River Garden and
wonderful friends. The
title, “Valued Volunteer”
truly fits our sweet, gentle
Naomie. She always
manages to say “yes,”
even when she was
recovering from surgery!
Hers is the pleasant voice
answering the Center
phones during staff
vacations. Her Southern
hospitality is well known
by our newest residents.
On behalf of all the members of the Jacksonville Jewish Center, the officers, board of directors and staff extend
heartfelt wishes of gratitude and mazel tov to these four outstanding ladies whose contributions enrich our lives.

Organizations
Center Choral Society
Jewish Singles
A great pasta & pizza party at Talie Bielski’s.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center provides
opportunities for Jewish singles from 21 to 35ish to gather
together for dinner and socializing a few times a month.
This group is open to all Jewish singles, regardless of
synagogue affiliation. This important program is sponsored
by the Center and, for the past two years, subsidized by
funding from the Jacksonville Jewish Federation. Flyers,
the Center Bulletin and the Jacksonville Jewish News notify
Jewish singles of upcoming activities. For more
information, and to join the group, call Rhoda at the Center
office, 292-1000.
55+ Club
Row 1 L to R: Molly Silverman, Pollie Copans, Sada Freedman,
Row 2 L to R: Jack Silverman, Philip Copans, Ben Edwards
The 55+ Club, now in its eleventh year, usually meets
the second Sunday of each month from 2 to 4 p.m. at the
Center. Programs include speakers, musical performers,
dancing exhibitions and interesting presentations. The enter¬
tainment is always exciting, refreshments are served and
there’s always time for socializing. The annual luncheon
in June is the highlight of the year. Membership is open to
the entire Jewish Community with annual dues only $12.50
per person.
For over 51 years, the Center Choir has been
enhancing services on the High Holidays and Shavuot with
moving liturgical music. Over the years they have given
numerous concerts featuring members of the choir as well
as nationally acclaimed soloists. Many of the current
members have been singing with this group for twenty years
or more. New members are always welcome.

Committees
Mitzvah Committee Membership
Joan Waitz, Chairperson Rhoda Goldstein, Chairperson
Bikkur Holim literally means “visiting the sick” and is a
religious imperative for us as Jews. The ancient tradition finds
its roots in a number of biblical and rabbinic texts.
In Bereshit, the first book of the Torah, we learn that
human beings are created b’tzelem Elohim, in God’s image.
Judaism understands this to mean that we are required to
emulate the ethical attributes of God, mercy, kindness,
forgiveness, graciousness.
Modern society with its wondrous advances in medical
technology, intimidating procedures and sterile hospital
environments, has, if anything, increased the need for Bikkur
Holim. The needs of the sick and aged require, not only the
best of scientific knowledge, but the loving care of family,
friends, neighbors and the synagogue community.
“To minister to the sick, is to minister to God.”
— Abraham Joshua Heschel
A special bouquet goes to Faye Price for her loyal visits
to Baptist Hospital. For more information and to volunteer
your time, call Joan Waitz, 731-2486.
Daily Minyan Captains
Traditionally, public worship requires a minyan, a
quorum of ten. Only in the presence of a minyan may the
Torah be read or the Kaddish prayer be recited.
Our dedicated minyan captains ensure that there is a
minyan twice every single day of the year. It is often a hard
and thankless job. It requires hours of phoning to coordinate
attendance.
It is because of them that you can recite kaddish when
you mourn or observe yarhzeit. We owe them not only our
thanks, but also our help, to continue providing a minyan.
Please call any minyan captain and become a “regular” for at
least one minyan a week.

The Center Membership Committee is committed to
extending friendship, recruiting, retaining and mostly
involving newcomers in the life of our congregation. This year
alone, over 60 new families have joined our ranks.
To meet the needs of our multifaceted Center family,
the Membership Committee provides a wide variety of
services, such as Shabbat synagogue greeters, hospital
visitation, newcomer welcome-bag delivery, outreach to
singles, and arrangements for holiday home-hospitality.
Since a family that “plays together, stays together”, the
committee sponsors brunches, casual dinners, cocktail parties
and other social events throughout the year.
Bringing our members together is the Membership
Committee’s greatest pleasure, and we welcome your ideas
and participation. Every member of our synagogue is
automatically a member our committee. Each of you is an
ambassador of good will, not only to new members, but to all
members. Together we can make the Center truly “the center
of our life”.
Henry Kramer Library and Resource Center
Visit the Henry Kramer Library and Resource Center.
It contains a rich collection of books of Jewish interest —
Bible, prayer, Talmud, Holocaust, philosophy, literature, Israel,
poetry, humor and fiction. All are available for reading by
members of our congregation.
The Library is open Sundays from 8:30 to noon.

the home of a family in mourning during the Shiva period. It’s still not the end of
the day because, as usual there’s a meeting at the Center that he must attend. This
has been his “easy day”.
Here it is Mit-Voch (Wednesday)
Things should be slowing down about now (wishful thinking). First thing
this morning there is a meeting with the staff to discuss up-coming events, such
as, Selichot, Rosh Hashanah, Yom Kippur and other issues of the day. Today is
also the day he delivers aD’var Torah at the Sisterhood Luncheon. Once a month
on Wednesday mornings, he leads a Sisterhood Seminar. When that is done he
returns to his office for a meeting with a Bar Mitzvah and his parents.
“We so much appreciate everything you did to make our sons Bar Mitzvah
so meaningful. Your generosity in allowing Rabbi Goldblum to give the sermon
Friday night, your warm comments at services about the family, your support and
friendship throughout the year, and more. — Mark and Beth Shorstein
The Beit Midrash Hebrew High is in session tonight and Rabbi Gaffney,
along with other educators and Rabbis from other congregations will be teaching.
This will be the 25th Confirmation Class he will guide through the confusing
maze of teen issues.
Rabbi Gaffney teaches the Confirmation
class of 1990 . . . with happy results.
“Confirmation Class gave me an opportunity to see how much you love to
teach. Going every Wednesday evening to your room was like opening a short
story — you never wanted it to end. The time passed by so fast. I will always
remember what you taught me. ” — Jason Schmerer
What’s Different about Thursday
Absolutely nothing is different — except more of it! At the morning minyan,
Rabbi Gaffney instructs an upcoming Bar Mitzvah in the “laying on” of tefillin.
No matter how many times he does this, the Rabbi enjoys this private moment
with the boy. Another generation is bound by a centuries old mitzvah. Later today,
Rabbi Gaffney travels to Gainesville to visit with our college students, and shares
with them news from home. He discusses with them religious questions and
encourages their comments. On his return, he prepares for his meeting with the
Executive Board. Then gets ready for meeting of the full board that evening. No
doubt about it, Rabbi David Gaffney is committed (and sometime thinks he should
be) to serving his congregation twenty-four hours a day.
"T-H-I-F” — Thank Ha’Shem It’s Friday
This is the home stretch. All the Rabbi has left to do is write his sermon for
Shabbat (You don’t think these speeches are the product of Divine providence,
do you?), compose his charge to the Bar or Bat Mitzvah, jot down some words of
welcome to out of town guests, get his announcement lists together— Now does
he get to rest as Shabbat begins on Friday night? It’s a day he enjoys most, but it
can’t be called restful. First there’s the early Kabbalat Shabbat.At a dinner hosted
by the parents of a Bar or Bat Mitzvah, he acts as emcee. Afterwards, it’s on to
the Friday evening service with it’s heart warming melodies like Lecha Dodi to
welcome the Sabbath, and the Kiddush. He would like to linger at the oneg Shabbat,
but he knows he must be up early tomorrow morning.

Confirmation
Celebrated 6 & 7 Sivan 5757 *May 30- June 1, 1998
The Biblical festival of Shavuot commemorates the giving of the Torah and Ten Commandments to the
Jewish people. It is natural that this festival should be celebrated with an accompanying sense of commitment to
Jewish life that Confirmation represents. Confirmands demonstrate the knowledge gained through the completion
of our Hebrew High program by full participation in Shavuot services.

Hebrew High School program. The following courses will be taught this

V’Dor - Generation to Generation, Introduction to Conversational
Hebrew, Hassidic Tales of the Holocaust, Judaism in Word and Deed,

Community Agencies
Jacksonville Jewish Federation
8505 San Jose Blvd. Jacksonville, FL 32217
448-5000 Fax.- 448-5715
The Jacksonville Jewish Federation
serves as a central resource for our Jewish
community. In summary, the Federation is
dedicated to providing for the welfare of
every Jewish person living in Jacksonville.
Through a partnership with the United
Jewish Appeal, we are equally committed to
the survival of and quality of life for every
Jew living in Israel and throughout the
Diaspora.
The four major local recipient agencies
of funds raised by the Federation are the
Jewish Community Alliance, Jewish Family
& Community Services, River Garden
Hebrew Home and the Jacksonville Jewish
Foundation. We are proud of the
invaluable services provided by these four
outstanding Jewish agencies. It is a privilege
to assist them in trying to meet their goals.
Jewish education is extremely
important and the Federation is proud to
support the Solomon Schechter Day School,
Beit Midrash Hebrew High, and Etz Chaim
Hebrew Academy. Through the Joan Levin
Gift of Israel program, Federation is helping
to make the dream of a trip to Israel a reality
for Jewish teens in our community.
The Federation is involved with com¬
munity relations, leadership development,
and Missions to Israel. We will continue
to work in cooperation with our local agen¬
cies, UJA and the synagogues to address
the vital issues and challenges in the en¬
tire arena of Jewish continuity. Our Board
wishes the members of the synagogue a
Happy & Healthy New Year.
As this Yearbook is dedicated to Rabbi
David Gaffney in honor of his 25 years of
service to the Jacksonville Jewish Center, we
would like to add our congratulations to Rabbi
Gaffney at this special moment in his career.
Rabbi Gaffney is a true friend of Federation
and his support is appreciated by our
leadership. It was a pleasure participating
with him on our Yom Ha’Atzmaut Mission
to Israel this past spring. Rabbi Gaffney’s
passion and devotion to all things Jewish
have allowed him to impact positively on his
synagogue and the. entire Jewish
community. A well deserved Mazel Tov to
him and his family!
Dr. Kenneth Sekine, President
Alan Margolies, Executive Director

Jacksonville Jewish Foundation
8505 San Jose Blvd. Jacksonville, FL 32217
448-5000 Fax.- 448-5715
The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation is dedicated to accumulating permanent
assets which can provide a source of income to help support the stability and
continuity of the Agencies and Synagogues in Jacksonville. The Foundation
professionally administers lifetime and testamentary giving plans designed to:
• Assist individuals to achieve their personal charitable goals in the most tax-
advantaged manner.
° Accumulate enduring endowed resources for use in supporting special,
emergency, and future needs; particularly those not provided for by the Jacksonville
Jewish Federation’s annual campaign.
The Foundation exists as a partnership of Jacksonville’s Synagogues and
Agencies to assure a better future for all generations. Through the Foundation,
donors are provided with many ways to perpetuate their charitable interests through
a wide array of funding opportunities.
In partnership with: Beth El-The Beaches Synagogue, Beth Shalom
Congregation, Congregation Ahavath Chesed (The Temple), Etz Chaim Synagogue,
Jacksonville Jewish Center, Jacksonville Jewish Federation, Jewish Community
Alliance, Jewish Family & Community Services and River Garden Hebrew Home.

Bonnie Sandler
Beth Shorstein
President
I am excited and proud to be taking over the reins of
the Center Sisterhood. Under the able guidance of Bonnie
Sandler, Sisterhood accomplished so much this past year. I
wish I could individually recognize all of the wonderful
members who carried out these activities, but I will, instead,
describe our many accomplishments.
The program theme this past year was “Women who
do Mitzvot in the Community.” We had a number of
wonderful speakers and inspiring entertainment, including
a creative night program. All of our fundraisers were
successful, including our second annual Simcha Showcase and Boutique, featuring
live music by Jacksonville’s klezmer band, Klezmania. The Holiday flower sales,
New Year’s cards, our fabulous bowling party, Nachas Tax, and Leagrams all added
to our fundraising efforts.
Our educational programs were stimulating, informative and appealing. We
are fortunate to have a large number of knowledgeable professional and lay people to
rely upon for our numerous activities. Book reviews, Israeli affairs arid social action
reports kept our members interested and informed. The Rabbi’s Sisterhood Seminars
and Sisterhood Bat Mitzvah classes contributed to our personal growth. Out of concern
for members of our congregation, we formed a bereavement committee, to help prepare
homes for the return of mourners following a funeral.
Sisterhood is very proud of its involvement with the Center’s youth groups. We
support these young people of our congregation in numerous ways, including providing
scholarships for all summer programs. On a national level, Sisterhood raises funds to
benefit students of the Jewish Theological Seminary, through our Torah Fund
campaign.
In the next few months, Sisterhood will continue doing all these wonderful
activities, and add some more. Plans are being discussed for new community service
projects; and closer to home, we are working to create closer relationships with our three school PTA’s. With their record
enrollments, they could use some extra help!
My incoming board is energized and full of new, innovative ideas. In order for our members to fully benefit, however,
they all need to become involved. Sisterhood offers something for everyone, whether it is creative handicrafts, programs,
social action, community service or Jewish Family Living. We all have strengths and talents that can be used to enhance our
Sisterhood, which, in turn, supports the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Find yourself in your Sisterhood. Let us support and
sustain it through our combined efforts.
Left: Attendees of Florida Branch Spring Convention,
May 1998, in Tampa. Right: Bonnie Sandler, bedouin
hostess at Branch “Salute to Israel” Dinner.

Salute to Israel Parade in New York - Starring Our Sixth Grade
(Reprinted from the Center Bulletin)
Dear liana,
The 34th Annual “Salute to Israel Parade”, which
this year celebrated the 50th Birthday of the State of Israel,
was the most exciting parade ever. With over 75,000
marchers and 3,000 spectators on each of the 25 blocks
of the parade route, the spirit of unity and pride was
overwhelming.
Our wonderful marching groups will be receiving
an official thank you and parade certificate in the weeks
to come. However, we could not let a week pass without
thanking the groups which made the success even sweeter,
namely our families who had the ultimate commute
packing up enthusiasm and joy, and most importantly, the
youth of their communities and flying into New York to
celebrate with us.
To have the students of Solomon Schechter of
Jacksonville, Florida carry their sunny message to the
people of New York, was a great honor for us, and
hopefully a great honor for your children as well.
There were many positive comments regarding the
level of dedication on the part of your school’s
leadership to encourage and contribute to this extra
special day.
We thank you from the bottom of our hearts.
TOD AH RABAH V’KOL HAKAVOD!
Best regards,
Qlwda JCaupnan
Creative Educational Coordinator and the entire Parade Staff

===== PAGE 65 =====
Administration
Executive Director’s Message
If you’ve walked through the
Jacksonville Jewish Center over the past
few months, you’ve noticed a lot of
refurbishing going on. We’ve had workmen
on the roof, in the kitchen, on the
campgrounds and in the classrooms.
We have new carpet in our sanctuary
and pre-school, handicapped access to our
bima, new restrooms in our day school and
new plumbing in our kitchen. There’s a new
security system and yes, we are even
working on the air conditioning.
We promised you these improvements as part of our
Centennial Challenge Campaign, and I am pleased to report
that we are moving straight ahead with plans to have our
facility renovated and our mortgage paid off in time for
the congregation’s Centennial Celebration in the year 2001.
In the midst of all of this construction, we are
planning another kind of refurbishment campaign at the
Jacksonville Jewish Center. This campaign does not require
another building fund pledge or any other additional
financial contribution. Rather it’s a refurbishment of our
Jewish spirit and soul.
This campaign is called “Shabbat — A Day for the
Rest of our Lives,” and its our congregation’s theme for
the coming year.
How appropriate it is that as we approach the new
millennium, and our congregation’s 100th birthday, we
rededicate ourselves to the observance and
experience of Shabbat, one of the most
central concepts of Judaism.
Shabbat has always been the
cornerstone of Jewish life. If we get more
of our members to engage in exploring
Shabbat, it will enhance their lives and, in
the process, unite us as a congregation and
a community.
Much of programming in the coming
year will be designed to help each of our
members experience personally the joy of
Shabbat. We look forward to your participation in this
exciting “refurbishment” project.
As I look back on this past year, I would like to
express my personal thank you to our many dedicated
professionals, staff, volunteers and lay leaders, who work
so diligently on behalf of the Jacksonville Jewish Center.
And to our members ... a special thank you for making
our congregation so vibrant and unique.
My family and I would also like congratulate Rabbi
David Gaffney for his 25 years of dedicated service to our
congregation and our community.
As we approach the New Year let us remember that
a refurbished building is nothing without a refurbished soul.
May the coming year bring each of us closer to one another
and closer to Shabbat.
On behalf of Edith, Sam and Max, Shana Tova.
— Bruce Horovitz
Bruce Horovitz
Executive Director
Activities Director’s Message
As I reflect on the events of the past year and peruse the calendar of events for this
coming year, I am proud and excited that every religious holiday, life cycle celebration,
lecture, luncheon, fundraiser, school or youth activity, gives us another opportunity to
showcase our achievements and strength.
Every year brings with it a new beginning. Each new administration brings new
ideas and fresh insight. One thing that remains constant, is that we at the Jacksonville
Jewish Center are a community and extended family, who share in the pleasure of
worshipping together and working together to support Jewish values. We not only celebrate
together, we are there for each other during times of stress and sorrow.
Our volunteers are a continual source of inspiration. They give their time and love to
our congregational family with unselfish devotion and we are grateful. We have so much
to offer and encourage everyone to become involved. This year let us all resolve to enhance our lives by reaching even
higher in the process of growing Jewishly.
On behalf of my family Abe, David & Talie, my best wishes for a year of health, happiness and peace. L’Shana Tova!
— Shirley Bielski
Shirley Bielski
Activities Director

Special Events
Simhat Torah Honorees
The High Holiday season reaches its joyous climax on Simhat Torah, the last day of the festival
of Sukkot. Because of our perennial love of the Torah, it has been referred to as Israel’s “bride”. On
Simhat Torah, we bring to a close the annual cycle of the reading of the Torah and immediately
begin anew. An ancient tradition evolved of honoring worthy men by calling them to the Torah for
the last reading, Hatan Torah, and the new beginning portion, Hatan Bereshit. In our synagogue
tradition, we also honor the contributions made by a “Woman of Valor”.
Nathan “Sonny” Sandler Mark Shorstein Martha Savage
Hatan Torah Hatan Bereshit Woman of Valor
Sonny is always
available to extend
a helping hand to
his friends and
neighbors. A
member of the
Center for more
than 50 years, he
has worked quietly
and without
publicity on behalf of the Center and
the Jewish community with
commitment, responsibility and
concern. A loyal and regular participant
of the daily Minyan, Sonny served as a
Minyan captain for twelve years. He
served on the Board, volunteered with
Day Camp and worked tirelessly on the
Bingo project in support of the Center.
He continues to serve as a member of
the Cemetery committee and can be
counted on annually to sell raffle tickets
to benefit our education programs.
A commitment Sonny takes very
seriously is his twenty year membership
in the Chevra Kaddisha. He has been
president for several years. No matter
what time of day he is called, Sonny is
available to perform the most reverent
mitzvah a Jew can do for his fellow man.
The members of the Chevra receive no
reward other than the inner satisfaction
for a service that is so vital to the
traditional Jewish community.
A man who is always busy, Sonny
has retired twice from Florida Paper
Company, yet still manages to work “part
time” 30 hours a week. A modest man,
he will allow his chest to swell on one
subject, his family. Sonny and Marilyn
have been married for 45 years, raised
four beautiful daughters, Arlene, Renee,
Suzy and Holly, and have six
grandchildren.
We were pleased to honor Sonny
for his significant contributions to our
synagogue and community.
Mark is a fifth
generation
Shorstein at the
Jacksonville
Jewish Center
and, like those
before him, has
become an integral
part of the Center’s
everyday life. Over the years, Mark has
conducted everything from Shabbat
services to the most critical financial
meetings with a sense of
professionalism and dedication that has
become synonymous with the Shorstein
name.
A true product of the Center,
Mark is a graduate of the Solomon
Schechter Day School, served as
president of USY and took an active
role in various youth activities. He is a
regular attendee of Monday morning
minyan and has even served the
congregation as an interim, lay cantor.
A graduate of University of
Pennsylvania’s Wharton School of
Finance, Mark is co-managing principal
of the well established CPA firm
Shorstein & Shorstein, PA.
Mark is the newly elected
president of the Center. As past vice-
president of Finance and chairman of
the Finance Committee, Mark’s
leadership and extraordinary accounting
talents were instrumental in keeping the
Center fiscally sound. As president, he
will be invaluable.
Mark’s community service is not
limited to the Center. Mark serves as
vice president of Jewish Family &
Community Services, is on the board
of the Jacksonville Jewish Foundation,
as well as the board of the Jacksonville
Art Museum.
Mark shared this honor with his
wife, Beth, children, Daniel, Rebecca,
Jennifer and Benjamin, as well as his
father, brothers and extended family.
her parents. Like
them, she was married at the Center and
like her children, she attended the
Center’s religious schools. As a young
bride she was a vice president of
Sisterhood and since has held many
positions of volunteer activity.
Because it is important to Martha
to make a difference she says, “I do
what I can, I don’t need a title!”
However there are many titles that
readily fit, such as, “fantastic fund¬
raiser, “official greeter,” “valued
volunteer”, an award given in 1995.
Martha is the person responsible for the
friendly faces that greet you on Shabbat
morning. She annually sells yearbook
greetings, Performing Artist
reservations, and Center Raffle tickets.
She is an “accomplished seamstress”,
who worked on the chuppah project, a
“pink lady” in charge of surgical
holding. The list goes on and on.
Martha has a vitality, that she
translates into action. A ticket seller
extraordinaire, 34 years ago she was
crowned Queer Esther for selling over
1,000 Purim program tickets and this
year her individual raffle ticket sales
raised more than $10,000 for Center
education programs.
We honored Martha for her
unselfish devotion to her synagogue,
family and friends. Proud mother and
grandmother, Martha exemplifies the
highest ideals Judaism by giving of
herself to help others Sharing her honor
were her children, Barry, Dona and
Doris, and granddaughters, Ashley and
Lara.

In Honor Of
^Rabbi ¿0AVID (Saffney
Dear Dad,
We would like to add our voices to the many who are extending their warm
congratulations to you on the occasion which marks your completing 25 years ... a quarter of
a century, with the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Your life has been intertwined with your
beloved congregation for a substantial portion of your life. You have, over the years, rejoiced
with those who celebrated happy and joyous events; shared with them in their personal
simchas and celebrated with them at the many milestones over which you have officiated.
You have also been with them in more difficult times, joining with them in prayer when
they were ill, counseling the troubled and comforting the bereaved. Always, you were available
to the Jewish Center membership, over weekends and into the late hours of night serving as
a rabbi in as large and as involved and as dynamic a congregation as is the Jacksonville
Jewish Center. You have always epitomized in your own spiritual life and in relation to your
congregants what a rabbi should be.
We know that you feel yourself to be truly a blessed man. Rabbinic life is not only a
profession for you — it is central to your personality. You love what you do with all your
heart* with all your soul and with all your might Your love for Torah, for Judaism, for the
Jewish people and for the State of Israel are boundless and your devotion to your congregation
has always been marked by mesirut nefesh, with a devotion that comes from your soul.
Teaching Jewish life... making people aware of the beauty and the depth of Jewish existence,
has always been an integral part of your personality. You have inspired people in countless
classes, with your thoughtful bulletin articles, in sermons and at every occasion when you
are given the opportunity to do what you love best — teach Torah. We have no doubt but that
the words found in the morning service “ashrenu, mah tovhelkenu” . . “how fortunate I am,
how good is our portion, how beautiful is our heritage, how happy we are to declare Sh ma
YIsrael...” are something that you affirm with your life.
You have always told us what a special synagogue the Jacksonville Jewish Center is
and how grateful you are for the respect, esteem and recognition that you receive. It has been
a very special shiddach, a wonderful match, from the first years that brought you to the
Jewish Center to the present time. We know how fortunate you feel in that you have had the
privilege of working with and for the finest and nicest people one can find in any congregation.
Regardless of how “all consuming” your work for the Jewish Center is we know you
have always given us all the attention that is possible, whether near or far. We do know that
your responsibilities were all embracing ... long evenings, meetings, Friday night through
Saturday night b’nai mitzvah, and classes on Sunday morning. You are blessed with a wife,
our beloved Mom, who has been so willing to share all this with you, most especially when
the line between public life and private life merge. You have also had in her a friend ... a
good counsel... a good listener ... and a woman who brought her own charm and poise to the
many friendships and relationships that you have enjoyed. She has truly been an ezerk’negdo,,
a helpmate at your side.
We are so proud that you are our father and we thank you much for being a role model
to us and our families. May you continue from strength to strength. We love you so much.
With great love and respect*
Aisher & Sabrina Shalva & David Jordana, Yoav Ezra and Shira

3e
• FAMILY COUNCIL
The adage “two heads are better than one” is born out in the development of the
Family Council. In 1987, the combination of Rabbi Gaffney’s desire to provide a vehicle
to increase parental involvement in their children’s religious education, and the creative
talents of Rabbi Dov Kentof to design the activities, resulted in a series of ten, hands-
on, family oriented programs, which were joyously well received. The program won a
program award at the 1988 United Synagogue Biennial Convention in only its second
year. Rabbi Gaffney will be the first to credit the continuing success of this program to
the innovative genius and hard work of Rabbi Kentof.
“Rabbi Gaffney was happy to see families working together, putting Judaism into
an active setting, where it is practiced to insure its continuation from generation to
generation. ” — Sue Ann Blumenthal
• MINYANAIRE
This Sunday morning program was especially attractive to men who could not attend
a weekday minyan. It began with services at 9 a.m., followed by breakfast and a guest
speaker or other presentation that Rabbi Gaffney arranged.
“It was the first Center activity that I got involved in that did not also involve my
wife. In that sense it was a precursor to the Men’s Club. It was fun, successful, and a
lot of fellows that were involved went on to become involved in other synagogue
and community projects. ” — Neil Sandler
Rabbi Gaffney’s sphere of interest, and influence, extends beyond the classroom
and sanctuary. He was instrumental in the development of many other projects,
organizations and programs, and helped to enhance still others.
Havurah groups
Ha-Rayim, young couples club
55+ Club, for seniors
The Center Men’s Club
Performing Artist Series
Henry Kramer Library
Congregational Summer Tours of Israel
HONORS
Rabbi Gaffney will brag openly about the accomplishments of his congregation,
but he has many award s to his credit.
• In 1976, elected Secretary of the Southeastern Region of the Rabbinical Assembly
by his colleagues. 1978, elected to serve as president, and the following year was
reelected to serve as president of the region.
• At the 1977 Biennial Convention of United Synagogues, Rabbi Gaffney presented
an outline describing the creative and significant ways in which the beliefs, values
and tradition of the Jewish people were highlighted through innovative worship and
ritual programs at the Center, and received for the Center, the prestigious Solomon
Schecter Award for Worship and Ritual.
• 1980 issue of “Who’s Who in American Jewry.”
• 1988, granted the honorary degree of Doctor of Divinity by the Jewish Theological
Seminary of America.
• 1989, appointed to the Board of Associates of the Center for Jewish Studies at the
University of Florida. He was asked to help plan the long range goals and suggest
ways to achieve these goals.
■ Sincere appreciation to Etta Drashin and Renee Gordon whose many
hours of work were invaluable to the success of this tribute.

Special Events
Annual Center Raffle for Education
A Citarice Encounter in Casab Canea".... A Nig fit to Remember1
The Center’s 1998 $10,000 Raffle to benefit education was a glitzy evening of casino-style gambling and dancing.
With over $52,000 raised, we all came out winners, especially our kids!
The evening had something for everyone. Larry Smith and his staff from Special Events by Confettis transformed
the Center into a Moroccan fantasy. Who could doubt we were in Casablanca? Over 600 attendees gambled in the
elaborate casino at “Cafe Americain”, danced to the music of the University of North Florida Jazz Combo and dined on
a sumptuous buffet prepared by the Center’s Catering Department.
Mr. Edward McCiamma was the winner of the $10,000 grand prize. Runner up prizes were awarded to: Mr. and
Mrs. Harold Bloom, Mr. and Mrs. Harry Frisch, Mr. and Mrs. Bruce Goldring, Mr. Wayne Hogan, Mr. and Mrs.
Doron Nevo, Mr. Bob Oullette, Mr. and Mrs. Sam Price, Mr. and Mrs. Leon Robbins and the Rogozinski Orthopedic
Clinic/Center for Physical Therapy. Shirley Bielski won a $100.00 gift certificate to Dillards during a random drawing
of the ticket seller’s. Congratulations also goes to Jack Selevan, the winner of our ‘Early Bird Special,” a weekend at a
luxury condo at Sawgrass. Fifty other lucky winners were awarded exciting casino prizes.
Gayle Bailys and Kathy Osterer, co-chairs, were delighted with the overwhelming response to this major fund¬
raising effort. Sincerest appreciation goes to First Union Bank and Special Events by Confettis for their generous
underwriting that made the evening fabulous. Thank you Grand Patrons, Patrons and all of you who purchased tickets.
Your support helped us reach a most impressive goal.
The support, devotion and many hours of hard work of the entire raffle committee, ticket sellers, Center staff,
friends and family ensured the continuation of quality programs for the youth of our congregation. We are so thrilled
and grateful to all of you. Thank you so much!
— Gayle and Kathy

Scouting
Cub Scout Pack 14
The 33 boys of Cub Scout Pack 14 had another
outstanding year at the Jacksonville Jewish Center,under the
leadership of Cubmaster Jim Richman. Some of our
activities included camping and winning many awards at the
Riverbend District Cubaree Camp out, Pinewood Derby
homemade car race at River Garden, Scout Shabbat, fishing
at River Garden, and our annual Blue and Gold Award
Banquet. We want to thank Jim as he completes his 7th year
of pack leadership.
The 5th grade Webelo den, along with den parent Stella
Finck, is to be commended on some special achievements.
The boys, Ori Demri, Ben Finck, Zachary Morris, David
Selber and Mathew Shorstein have achieved the highest rank
in Cub Scouting — The Arrow of Light, as well the Aleph
Award, the religious emblem that our pack has not seen earned
in quite a few years. Congratulations to the boys and their
families.
Our 2nd grade group was led by Elissa Vining (along
with the Pack Mascot-Sparky Vining). These boys earned
their Wolf badge and enjoyed many activities. Good work
Cubs — Adam Friedman, Mathew Glassman, Stefan
Mykych, Kevin Norton, Zachary Schemer, Brian Sherman,
Kyle Solloway, Cameron Spiritas and Kyle Vining.
The 3rd grade den worked very hard this year. Their
den parents Beth Shorstein, Deena Richman, and Jeri
Schwartz helped their boys to earn the Bear badge and many
gold and silver arrows. Hats off to David Denman, Jack
Joseph, Brian Levenson, Louis Richman, Jonathan Sandler,
Sam Schwartz, Amie Silverberg, Benjamin Shorstein, Adam
Weiss, Joseph Yarish and Josh Rosenberg.
Our 4th grade Webelos were also led by Elissa Vining
with Stacy Epstein. These boys earned many Webelo pins
and are well on their way to fulfilling the requirements for
The Arrow of Light. These boys are Aaron Blankstein,
Michael Epstein, Josh Fleet, Michael Meisel, Jonathan
Mizrahi, David Richter, Kyle Schoettler and Andrew Vining.
This was my seventh and final year as Pack 14
Committee Chairperson. Ori has crossed over into Boy Scouts,
thus joining my other son Michael. I would like to take this
opportunity to thank the Center staff for all their assistance
and cooperation. Thanks to Anne Depaul, our Unit
Commissioner, to Carole Goldberg for her instruction, all the
parent leaders and volunteers, and most of all, a very special
thanks to Jim Richman. Without having Jim along for the ride,
I would have had to have stopped the train and gotten off long
ago!!!!
GO MIGHTY CUB SCOUTS OF MIGHTY PACK 14!!
Cindy Demri

Solomon Schechter Day School
We, of the Solomon Schechter Day School of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center, welcome a new year with the
largest enrollment in our thirty-seven year history. The school
now has three Kindergarten Classes and double classes through
the fourth grade. In addition, we have expanded our Middle
School Program to include the seventh grade.
The school is utilizing every square foot of educational
space in the building available to it. Our classrooms are
dynamic places where careful attention is given to individual
learning styles and group sizes and teaching approaches are
varied so each child will be reached. A dedicated faculty leads
students through an enriched curriculum in which texts are only one source of information.
The richness of Jewish tradition permeates the school day. Through observance of daily prayer
and kashrut, in holiday observances, and through teaching of Mitzvot, Judaica becomes an integral
part of everyday life. Hebrew language study goes beyond just being a language program with the
goal of fluency.
Now we turn our vision to the future. We look forward with much
anticipation to the continued process of creating, together with our parents,
students and members of the congregation’s leadership, a school which
is truly educationally significant.
The Solomon Schechter Day School looks back with gratitude to
all those who sustained it during the early years, are maintaining its
identity today, and looks forward with confidence and enthusiasm to the
years ahead.
Evelyn Borstein
— Willard Kennedy School Secretary
Willard M. Kennedy
Principal

===== PAGE 127 =====
Youth Activities
Summer Programs for Jewish Youth
Gamp Ramah Palmer and Ramah Darom
The Jacksonville Jewish Center is very fortunate to have a large representation
of youngsters participating in the Camp Ramah programs both in New England and
the new Ramah Darom in Georgia. Ramah, an arm of the Conservative Movement,
offers a wonderful summer opportunity for informal enrichment and meaningful
education.
Attending Camp Ramah Palmer in New England were: Rachel Gerber, Sara
Mizrahi, Aliza Morris, Melissa Osterer, Ashley Osterer, Rachel Rosner, Amy
Schuster, Rebecca Shorstein, Jonathan Tannen, Ashley Torres, Shayna Weiss
and Alex Whitman.
Attending Ramah Darom in Georgia were: Josh Appelbaum, Geri Bernard,
Ori Demri, Ben Finck, Ari Friedman, Cara Goldberg, Annie Levenson, Faye
Maiman, Lauren Margol, Dena Mizrahi, Lindsay Morris, Zach Morris, Lauren
Richter, Erin Rogozinski, Ben Rogozinski, Josh Rogozinski, Jessica Rogozinski,
Adam Rosner, David Selber, Jennifer Shorstein, Benjamin Shorstein, Benay
Shorstein and Mathew Shorstein.
Our thanks to the families and organizations which provide Ramah
Scholarships: Center Sisterhood, Abe Selber Trust Fund, Myra Thier Lazarus
Ramah Fund and Robert Gordon Scholarship Fund.
U.S.Y. on Wheels
This fine program gives teenagers
an opportunity to travel around the
United States seeing landmarks,
historical sites and National parks. In
addition they meet Jewish youth in the
cities in which they stay. This year Josh
Bernard, Aaron Finck, Jessica
Osterer, Jesse Rauchwager, Sara
Sekine, Drew Shenkman, Daniel
Shorstein and Esther Yegelwel joined
other U.S.Y.ers on Wheels.
USY Israel/Poland Pilgrimage and Ramah in Israel
This is a unique opportunity for young people ages 15 to 18 to visit Israel.
Based in Jerusalem each of our groups travels the country experiencing their Jewish
heritage. In addition to spending a delightful summer with their Israeli peers, our
“pilgrims” also develop lifelong friendships with their traveling companions from
the United States and Canada. An additional tour of Poland gives a deeper
understanding of the Holocaust. Center USYers who went on Pilgrimage were
Jonathon Cohen, Eli Fleet and Alyssa Rademan. Jeffrey Glassman attended
Ramah in Israel, and Shira Morris and Natalie Osterer went to Poland and Prague
as well as Ramah in Israel.

Community Organizations
American Red Magen David
Founded in 1930 as a First Aid Society, Magen David
Adorn has become the State of Israel’s emergency medical,
disaster, ambulance and healthcare network. 365 days a year,
24 hours a day, every person in every corner of Israel looks to
MDA to perform the usual tasks carried out by Red Cross
Societies throughout the world. Within minutes, MDA’s rescue
units arrive on the scene for medical emergencies, accidents
and, unfortunately, terrorist bombings. Trained paramedics
administer immediate help and then transport the patient to
the hospital if necessary.
Even though the symbol of Magen David Adorn, a red
star of David, is recognized by the American Red Cross, efforts
are still going on to achieve international acceptance of our
symbol.
As part of our continuing efforts to raise every possible
dollar, we have arranged for anyone, who can, to donate their
car, van, motor home or boat, running or not, to benefit
ARMDI. (It’s fully tax deductible). Call (800) 550-3333 and
mention ARMDI for details and/or pick-up.
You can show your support for the State of Israel for
only $18 (Chai), and do the mitzvah of pikkuach nefesh by
joining today.

Brandéis University
National Women’s Committee
The purpose of the Brandéis University National
Women’s Committee is to provide financial support and
growth for the Brandéis University Libraries, which serve a
community of students and scholars, in education and
research, united by their commitment to the pursuit of
knowledge. The National Women’s Committee offers its
members opportunity for intellectual pursuit, continuing
education, community service, social interaction, personal
enrichment, and leadership development. The members act
as emissaries to support and enhance the image of Brandéis,
a Jewish-sponsored, non-sectarian university where
excellence is the tradition.
For more information, call Norman Levy, 273-1575.

Finally it’s Shabbat Morning
Rabbi Gaffney “qvels” as David
Goldberg reads from the Torah.
"IVken 9 jjiMi came tc [jaekdcm-
<mUc ad an addidiauf íhJsJñ
Qa^neif made a dfoeclal e^odt to-
Include me, and to- muitune me cud
