jjCUtkjfui, but jfMÍ and jj&iemodt, a
mendch, a dendltlae, ccuUncf and
ccmfKiddlanate human bemcf. "
—Rabbi Michael Matuson
Rabbi Gaffney is always an
eloquent speaker.
This morning he presides over services with a large congregation of
“regulars”, and an even larger shul because there’s a simcha. He explains the
Torah portion and then watches proudly as the Bar Mitzvah puts on his talit for
the first time. He always qvels from a beautiful Bar or Bar Mitzvah who participates
by reading from the Torah and chanting a flawless haftorah. For him it is one of
the perks of the job. After the service there’s a Kiddush Luncheon, and then he
participates in a Torah study group at the home of Eddie and Judy Mizrahi. By
then, it’s time to return to the Center for the mincha service, with it’s special
nusach to signal the end of the Shabbat. Before Maariv he partakes of the Shalosh
Seudot, and raises his voice in singing a variety of Hebrew and folk melodies.
There’s always an interesting gem of Torah imparted, followed by the Birchat
Hamazon.
“On Shabbat evening, at Shalosh Seudot, Rabbi Gaffney, myself, and everyone
else who attends, shares many wonderful times singing and laughing around the
table, and studying a “ ‘bissel” Torah with Rabbi. There is never a dull moment, and
every word is a pearl, never to be forgotten. I have learned so much from him about
Judaism, Jewish life, and life in general. The knowledge is priceless.
— Mathew Schmerer
Then it’s time for Maariv and the beautiful Havdalah service. That’s still not
the end of the day. When there’s a Bar Mitzvah party, Rabbi David Gaffney is
there ‘til the last Israeli dance. Finally, it’s time to go home at the conclusion of
his “day of rest.”
It’s Sunday ... IT STARTS ALL OVER AGAIN...
Glimpses of the Milestones and Accomplishments
of the past 25 Years
Twenty-five years ago the Board of Directors of the Jacksonville Jewish Center
announced the appointment of Rabbi David Gaffney as the spiritual leader of our
congregation. He arrived, along with his wife Inge and their two children, Asher and
Shalva, to begin a journey of inspiration and continuing accomplishments that would
propel our congregation to the forefront of the Conservative movement.
Just four years later, Rabbi Gaffney would help plan one of the most exciting
events in the history of the Jacksonville Jewish Center — the move from Third and
Silver, the home of the Center for nearly fifty years to Crown Point Road, the new home
of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. It was done with all the pomp and ceremony befitting
such an auspicious occasion. A caravan of cars left Third and Silver to escort the
Torah scrolls replete with all their trapping to be placed in the Ark in their new home.
Rabbi Gaffney, Center President Charles Mizrahi and Cantor Marton, each of them
holding a Torah scroll, led the procession from the deck of a flatbed truck
“As we look to the future, we also must learn from our past. We had a dream ...
it came into being because of the foresight of our synagogue leaders. With the complete
furnishing of our building, the dream will be completed. Our dream will once again
become a reality. —Rabbi Gaffney
Just as the leaders of our new synagogue planned for its growth and improvement,
so, too, Rabbi Gaffney planned for the spiritual and educational growth and improvement
of its congregants.
His devotion to all things Jewish is reflected the abundance and diversity of the
programs he has initiated.
The following is but an overview of the programs we now enjoy because of the
foresight of Rabbi Gaffney.

Day School/PreSchool PTA
“The very world rests on the breath of children in the schoolhouse.” —Talmud
It is with this in mind that our parents, teachers and administrators work together to
insure an enriched education for our children. For 20 years, PTA’s successful magazine sale
has played a significant role in funding excellent programming, equipment and materials. This
past year PTA provided the new preschool playground equipment, the computerization of the
Henry Kramer Library and Resource Center, and music education materials.
Some of the many services and activities sponsored for our students include:
• Shabbat Boxes - taken home each Friday by one student in every class • Kaleidoscope - an
entire day devoted to the arts • Red Ribbon Week - drug awareness program • Vision Screening
• Library Assistants - parents volunteer to help students and librarian • Holiday Observances
- help with students’ celebration of Rosh Hashanah, Chanukah, Tu B’Shevat, Purim, and
Passover • Picture Lady - art appreciation for Pre-K, Kindergarten, and First graders • Mystery
Reader - a new storytelling program for Pre-K and Kindergarten • Much, much more.
Thank you for supporting your PTA through your numerous volunteer hours and financial
assistance. Looking forward to working with you in 98-99!
— Arlene Yegelwel

===== PAGE 155 =====
Impressions of Rabbi David Gaffney
on the occasion of his Silver Jubilee at the Jacksonville Jewish Center
by Raymond Cohen
How do you measure twenty-five years? Do you simply count the number of
years — 25 of them... the months— 300. Do you merely count the days — 4260.
Or, do you measure twenty-five years in the contributions, the accomplishments, the
deep concern, the inspiration, the impact Rabbi Gaffney has made on the lives of our
congregation. To paraphrase the words of the Ethics of the Fathers, it is measured in
his “love of Torah, divine service, and the practice of loving kindness between him
and his flock.”
Who is Rabbi Gaffney
The Rabbi is a person just like you. He puts his talit on, one shoulder at a time, but
that’s where the comparison ends. You might think all he does is deliver a sermon once
a week on Shabbat. Nothing could be further from the truth. Here is a typical week in the
life of Rabbi David Gaffney.
It’s Sunday — the week begins
The Rabbi has just returned home from the morning minyan followed by his Talmud
class and Beginner’s Judaism class, and is on his way out to play golf. Not likely. In fact,
more than likely, his phone is ringing. He answers it, and the person on the other end
sounds frantic and distraught. Someone close has passed away suddenly. Does the Rabbi
say “take two prayers and call me in the morning.”? No. He hangs up the phone and goes
directly to the home of the person who called, and expresses his condolences. He does
what he does so well, he comforts the family. He talks to them about the deceased. He
helps them understand their grief. He answers their questions, such as, how long the
shiva period lasts or what the mourning period is for a parent or a sibling.
“Today, on the eve of Debbie's yartzeit, I am determined to gather the strength to
properly convey our appreciation to you. Speaking of strength, I can't think of anyone
else (besides our dedicated doctors) who was always there at the right time to help us
carry our burden. From the moment we first learned of Debbie's illness, when you where
there at University Hospital, to your visit with us at Albert Einstein in New York, and
your appearance at out home, just after she took her last breath, your presence and
concern helped us carry on. " — Carole Katz
It’s still Sunday
After Rabbi Gaffney returns from the bereavement call, he is off to the cemetery
for an unveiling. After that he must prepare for an evening wedding. One life ends, but
there is a new beginning for a happy young couple.
“Throughout the many years I have known you, you've treated me like a special friend.
From the beautiful words you spoke at my wedding, to the beautiful, inspiring words you
wrote me in your kind letter, you have a knack for making me feel so terrific, and so lucky to
be the recipient of your encouragement and warmth." — Karen Baumgarten Sher

===== PAGE 161 =====
Scouting
Daisy Troop 258
This past year, Daisy Troop 258 was the largest group of girls
the Jacksonville Jewish Center has hosted. These very special young
scouts learned how to sew, weave, cook and create some unique
projects for a group of five year olds.
Also, the troop participated with the Brownies in baking
hamantaschen and mishloach manot baskets for the residents of
Mt. Carmel, at Purim. A pool party was held at Epping Forest, to
wrap up a very busy year.
Among the valuable lessons learned through the Daisy program, learning the meaning of friendship and
doing mitzvot in the community were brought out through a variety of
activities.
This Daisy Troop will continue at the
Center under new leadership, as we will be
moving up to become Brownie leaders. We
know the Daisy scouts will continue with a
great program in the future
— Lynn Kluger and Beverly Eagerton
Brownie Troop 882
Brownie Troop 882 had a wonderful and fulfilling year. We earned
many new Try-its from each of the five worlds: the World of the Arts, the
World of the Out-of-Doors, the World of People, the World of Well-Being,
and the World of Today and Tomorrow. And that’s not all! We went on
field trips to River Garden, Pelotes Island, a variety of local businesses,
and Mt. Carmel. We also went on two special campouts this year. One
was in Seminole Springs, where we saw Indian tents and panned for gold.
The other was at our own Camp Chowenwaw. Both times gave us the opportunity to try out all the camping
skills we had been working on for months ahead of time.
Of course, we also participated in the annual Girl Scout cookie sale — and boy, did we sell cookies! After
a banner sale, the girls earned enough to take a fun trip to Adventure Landing’s water park. There was even
some money left over to donate to a charity. The third graders finished off the year with a special trip to
Savannah, the birthplace of Juliette Lowe, the founder of Girl Scouting. On the first day we camped at Skidaway
National Park. The second day was spent touring both of her homes and her burial site. This was a trip to
remember!
Shirley and Beth are both leaving Troop 882, admittedly with some
regrets. Shirley will be a co-leader of Junior Troop 5, and Beth is assuming
the presidency of the Center Sisterhood. We leave Brownie Troop 882 in
the able hands of Beverly Eagerton and Lynn Kluger. All girls in 1st
through 3rd grades are encouraged to join. You won’t regret it!
— Beth Shorstein and Shirley Jemigan

They tell of Adam:
How frightened he must have been when
for the first time
he saw the sun disappear,
ending the light of day.
It was Adam’s first darkness!
How could he understand the night,
when he had never seen a dawn?
After the splendor of the sun,
how astonishingly dark the darkness was;
how desperate the long terror
of the first fall of night...
until Adam learned day would come again:
that there is order in the universe.
And he could begin to see
how much light remains in the sky at night:
the stars, and their enduring promise of the sun.
The returning star of day.
Adam learned
the night is never wholly dark;
and no night is endless...
even as each of us must leam it
in our own times of trouble and of darkness.
The light is never far.
Adam's story is our story:
Certainly, there is much that is
dark and wrong in the world today
and in ourselves:
meanness, anguish, brutality,
greed, frustration, despair.
Yet always there is also order
and goodness in the world and in ourselves:
love, courage, sacrifice, creativity,
growth, dedication, regeneration.
In the midst of chaos and change,
whatever may have been changed into evil
can be changed again into goodness,
whether it be a moment or an era.
There is always an order and a permanence
to which we can relate ourselves,
even as one may look up
to the permanence of the sky.
We have been given the power and responsibility
to live our life as if the scales
of what is right and wrong in the world
were exactly balanced,
and our actions change this balance.
To leam how to live this way is not easy.
The occasional impulse toward goodness
is not enough.
To meet the challenge of a fulfilled life,
we must train ourselves
to the habit of goodness,
to the continuing act of goodness...to mitzvot
at every moment of choice we have.
This power to train ourselves
is one of the greatest of all the powers of Man.
And there are many people -
in the present and of the past -
who can help us develop it.
We are not alone.
The decision is ours to make,
but the achievement is with others.
We are not alone,
and the light is never far.
“I would despair if
7 did not see the goodness
of the Lord in the land of the living ’ ” *

Bruce Adler
Sunday, October 26, 1997
Often described as a “Yiddish”
Danny Kaye, Bruce Adler is a
highly seasoned showman. The son
of Yiddish vaudeville legends,
Julius Adler and Henrietta
Jacobson, Adler is an exuberant,
joyful, power-packed talent who
can do anything from a knee-
rupturing Russian kazachok, to Gene Kelly’s umbrella-swinging
choreography from Singin ’ in the Rain, without losing an ounce of his
dazzle. Adler’s performance was sensational.
Jon Simon
Sunday, January 11, 1998
Jazz pianist Jon Simon was featured
in a cabaret-style performance. One
of America’s foremost contemporary
Jewish musical artists, Simon has
released several recordings that have
captivated audiences worldwide.
His masterful technique and
incredible improvisational skills are
truly extraordinary. Simon’s concert
was filled with heartfelt and humorous interpretations of songs we all
know and love, coupled with stories, anecdotes and humor.
Neshama Carlebach
Sunday, February 15,1998
Songstress Neshama Carlebach
follows in the tradition of her late
father, Rabbi Shlomo Carlebach.
Neshama’s talent and charisma
have endeared her to audiences
throughout the world. While
following in her father’s footsteps,
she has the unmistakable Carlebach
depth of soul and the ability to captivate, yet she has her own unique
artistic style. With a powerful voice that easily spans several octaves,
she is a natural-bom performer. She was electrifying.

Early Childhood
Message from the Director
Early Childhood Department
Located in the Selevan Pre-School
■■i
Dale Schemer
Director
The Jacksonville Jewish Center Early Childhood Department
has enjoyed a reputation as one of the best in Jacksonville for many
years. Our dedicated staff is extremely proud of the excellent
educational programs we provide our students. Our environment is
structured to provide students the opportunity to grow socially,
emotionally, physically, and creatively as well as intellectually.
and
Our Pre-School also offers group instructions that enhance our
daily schedules. Our Judaic program includes education in the
fundamentals of Jewish life and Torah with emphasis on weekly Shabbat
holiday celebrations. Our Physical Education and Music classes are favorites of every age group.
This year promises to be an exciting adventure for everyone involved. We look forward to adding
innovative new programs for our children, parents and staff.
We have many things to be proud of and we would love an opportunity to share them with you. You
are welcome to come and tour our Pre-School anytime.
Playground pais
Junior firefighters.
Shabbat Shalom!
67
===== PAGE 173 =====
Rhoda Goldstein and Janis Dorman
who serve this congregation
faithfully and loyally.
If gratitude is the essence of
my reflections I need, especially, to
express hakarat ha-tov ...my
gratefulness to lay leaders whose
devotion and dedication to this
synagogue is so extraordinary. We
can be proud of the fact that we
are one of the finest congregations
in the country. I find it more than
fortuitous that I should be writing this
message as a new
administration, led by our
President Mark Shorstein
takes office. I can recall, as
if it were yesterday, the
warmth and cordiality with
which an invitation to serve
this congregation as its rabbi
was extended by Jack
Shorstein and his beloved
Sylvia, may her name be for
a blessing. Jack introduced
me to a group of leaders who
were conscientious and
devoted to the well-being of
our synagogue and to Jewish
life. It is extraordinary that
we have come full circle -that a
generation has passed and Jack and
Sylvia’s son Mark serves now as
president. That he is joined by his
beloved Beth who is president of our
always dynamic Center Sisterhood,
is especially meaningful to me.
Over these twenty-five years
I have had the pleasure of serving
with thirteen different congregational
presidents -Jack Shorstein, Charles
Mizrahi, Sheldon Gendzier,
Lawrence DuBow, Nate Krestul, Sol
Proctor, Dr. Joseph Honigman, Gene
Kornblum, Marcia Pollock, Jeff
Morris, Stuart Hecht, Evan Yegelwel
and now Mark Shorstein. These
devoted individuals represented a
large group of Center officers,
supporters and volunteers whose
hearts were moved in their
understanding of the needs of our
congregation.
Whatever my achievements,
nothing would have happened
without their help. Together we
were able to move this congregation
from its facility on 3rd and Silver in
the Springfield area to the beautiful
campus we have at our present
location. Together, with their
devotion and the financial support of
people of vision, we have built an
outstanding and beautiful synagogue
to serve our needs. Together we
expanded on the programs of our
Solomon Schechter Day School, our
afternoon Hebrew school and our
youth programs. Over the years
every initiative that I was prompted
to consider in my concern for the
needs of our membership was
supported and encouraged by our
lay leaders. We are a congregation
devoted to its religious traditions.
We have minyan services every
morning and evening every day of
the year. The changes we have
made with regard to the participation
of all of our members at services
were made with a view towards
change with discretion. We
continue to maintain a fundamental
focus of the importance of education
and our youth. We have also
expanded our education programs to
serve adults. We have enjoyed
years of Adult B’nai Mitzvah
classes, Sisterhood Seminars, Torah
Study classes, and Talmud classes.
From the pulpit and from the podium,
I was encouraged to teach. We
have personalized our large and
active synagogue by urging
membership in havurot, by creating
programs like the minyannaires, and
by encouraging the formation of the
Center’s Men’s Club to complement
a most active and dynamic Center
Sisterhood. We have opened our
congregation and community to the
world of Jewish culture with our
Performing Artists Series.
We have been challenged,
both intellectually and
emotionally, with many
scholars who shared our
Shabbaton and we have been
informed about the
fundamental issues that
effect the Jewish community
through our Setzer-Levit
programs. Our concerns are
all encompassing ...from the
youngest child to the mature
members of our
congregation who enjoy our
55+ programs and the many
other activities that we offer.
I could not have effected any
of the above were it not for the
cooperation, support and the
sensitivity on the part of our lay
leadership who trusted my instinct
as to what our congregational needs
were.
My personal thank you to those
who made possible, in this edition of
the yearbook, this most loving
expression of my twenty-five years
as your rabbi — Peggy Organes,
Raymond Cohen, Etta Drashin,
Renee Gordon and her committee,
Susan Letherman and Shirley
Bielski.
If I reflect on my blessings I
need to add my gratitude to a loving
wife who was always patient,
understanding and sensitive to the
demanding schedule of a rabbi who
serves a large congregation. I always
enjoyed Inge’s counsel and support;
6

===== PAGE 176 =====
Organizations
Center Men’s Club
The Jacksonville Jewish Center Men’s Club provides an opportunity for our
Center men to work together supporting, sponsoring and participating in programs
that bring meaning to our youth, companionship to our elders, and involvement in
our community.
Through active membership in the Federation of Jewish Men’s Clubs, an
international organization dedicated to the ideals, philosophy and traditions of
Conservative Judaism, we distribute hundreds of yellow Holocaust Memorial
candles to our congregation’s families every Yom Hashoah. This year we will
present the Federation program “Hearing Men’s Voices,” a series of workshops
devoted to creating a forum for discussion and sharing of issues relating to being
a Jewish man in today’s world. Thought provoking topics in the areas of family, religion, society and health will be
covered.
The Men’s Club is committed to Center youth. We provide support and help with youth conventions and
activities. We present every Bar and Bat Mitzvah with the Shabbat Seder, a book published by the Federation of
Jewish Men’s Clubs, as well as presenting the Youth Leadership Award to outstanding Confirmation students each
Shavuot. This year, we were especially proud to introduce the Yad Shel Chai (Hand of Life) award program which
encourages and rewards post Bar/Bat Mitzvahs who continue reading Torah on Shabbat, holidays and at minyan.
Teens are rewarded for reading a minimum of 18 portions by age 18 with a beautiful, inscribed Torah pointer (yad).
This year four boys were recognized for this achievement: Seth Finck, Mark Frisch, David Organes and Jonathan
Tannen. Those interested in this program may contact Randall Smith for more information.
In our community, we bring companionship to elders with the River Garden Fishing Day, enhance support
programs with contributions to the Federation and JFCS , and volunteer each Christmas to allow our friends of
other faiths to celebrate their holiday with their families.
We are visible friends of our Center as well. Each year we sell and build sukkot for individual families, decorate the
congregation’s Goldman Sukkah, cook at the Lag B’Omer picnic, usher at Shabbat and
Holiday service, and participate in and
sponsor kiddushes on Men’s Club and
Armed Forces Shabbats We provide
several Sunday speaker brunches,
coffee tastings and how-to clinics. We
have won Torch Awards for
outstanding programs from the
Federation of Jewish Men’s Clubs.
Happy sukkah customers.
The Men’s Club is also a great
way for friends to meet and have fun. Just join us every summer for
the infamous deep sea fishing trip or bring your family with us to a
Lizard Kings hockey game and a Jacksonville Suns baseball game.
All this and more is waiting you, if you are at least 21, male and a
member of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Join us now.
— Dave
The best fishing trip yet!

Community Agencies
iewish Family & Community Services
3601 Cardinal Point Drive
Jacksonville, FL 32257-5582 • Phone 448-1933
Iris T. Young Executive Director
Jewish Family & Community Services is proud to meet the changing needs of the
Jewish community. In the past year alone, the agency has improved its ability to serve
the community by adding some exciting new initiatives to its diverse menu of programs.
Planned Lifetime Assistance Network
PLAN enables individuals to arrange for the future care of themselves or their loved
ones. Children of aging parents or relatives of disabled individuals can contract with
JFCS to ensure that the financial and social needs of these individuals are met throughout
the course of their lives.
Senior Transportation
JFCS still transports seniors to religious services, doctor appointments, shopping centers
and recreational activities for a very affordable fee. The Shalom Shuttle and Mitzvah
Mobile are air-conditioned, handicap-accessible buses operated by courteous,
professional drivers who provide door-to-door service.
Bus Rental
Now the community can rent the JFCS buses to shuttle guests to and from life cycle
events and family gatherings. Enjoy bar and bat mitzvahs, weddings and other special
occasions without the headache of coordinating rides for out-of-town guests.
Community Kosher Nutrition Program
For approximately 20 years, seniors in our community have enjoyed hot, well-balanced
kosher meals prepared by the CKNP In addition to serving nutritious and delicious
food at Mt. Carmel, the program provides a safe and friendly environment where diners
can socialize while they eat.
Catering Service
With so much experience preparing good food, JFCS now caters brunches, engagement
parties, bar and bat mitzvahs and other life cycle events. Just For You Catering Services
provides delicious food, tastefully presented, while observing dietary laws.
Adoption
JFCS continues to place babies into loving homes across the country. The agency is
licensed to place children in Florida, Connecticut and New York, three states that require
a license. Last year we found adoptive families for approximately 70 babies.
Counseling
JFCS provides quality mental health care by qualified professionals at reasonable rates.
Confidentiality is always guaranteed. The caring staff offers a wide range of services
for individuals, couples and families, including pre-marital counseling, divorce mediation,
custody home studies, grief counseling and family counseling just to name a few. Most
insurance plans are accepted.
Feed A Needy Neighbor
With donations of non-perishable food items from a concerned community, JFCS provides
emergency groceries to families and individuals experiencing difficult times. The agency
has never had to turn a hungry person away thanks to ongoing support, from the
community.

Mount Carmel
Gardens, Inc.
5846 Mt. Carmel Terrace
Jacksonville, FI. 32216
(904)733-6696
Linda Rubens, R.N., N.H.A.
Executive Director
Home Is Where The Heart Is
Mount Carmel Gardens apart¬
ments was designed, even to the
smallest detail, to provide comfortable
and pleasant surroundings. From the
initial concept, Mt. Carmel Gardens has
strived to create respectable living for
the elderly community, providing more
than housing. Mt. Carmel Gardens offers
a 17-story building on a beautifully
landscaped site, 24-hour staffing,
community facilities, and planned
programs, all of which were developed
as part of an over-all concept.. .a concept
of responding to the desires of retirees
for security, comfort, safety,
independence and the enrichment of
stimulating social-recreational activities
shared with others.
Mount Carmel Gardens is conve¬
niently located, with transportation,
shopping, hospital and doctor’s offices
nearby.

Committees
Shabbat Greeters
Martha Savage, Chairperson
Martha Savage coordinates the
friendly volunteers who give of their
time to perform the mitzvah of
welcoming people to services with a
friendly “Shabbat Shalom”. Greeting is
a good way to introduce yourself to
people and make newcomers and
visitors feel welcome. We thank Martha
for her dedication to the Center and to
all of the people who volunteered to
greet over the past year. Anyone
interested in joining the Shabbat
Greeters, please call Martha .
High Holiday Preparation
Shabbat Ushers
Coordinated by the Men’s Club
Every Shabbat and holidays these
friendly volunteer members serve as
ambassadors to Center congregants,
helping with seating, guiding and
acknowledging newcomers, and
welcoming regular worshippers. Ushers
help to maintain synagogue decorum
which preserves the beauty of the service
for all of us. We thank all of our ushers
for their efforts throughout the year.

Shabbat Torah Readers
Ted Gross, Coordinator
Psalm 91 has been called the
“Psalm of Afflictions.” The psalmist
lists every manner of affliction from
which God delivers those who trust in
Him. The last line is repeated to make
the number of lines equal to 17, the total
numerical value of the letters in the word
tov, good, (9 + 6 + 2).
Our society faces many
afflictions. Devotion to Torah and
participation in its regular readings will
help us to cope with these difficulties.
We are therefore thankful to the large
number of students who have chosen to
emphasize Torah Reading as an
essential aspect of the Bar/Bat Mitzvah
procedure.
We thank our highly-qualified on¬
going readers and those who joined
the team during the past year: This
year’s readers included:
Josh Appelbaum, Daniel Benrubi,

Community Agencies
Jewish Community Alliance
8505 San Jose Blvd. • Jacksonville, FL 32217
Phone: (904) 730-2100 • Fax: (904) 730-2444
— Board of Directors —
Executive Committee
Irene Jaffa

Howard L Korman
Past Board Presidents
Over the past 10 years, we have continued to grow and change, to strengthen
our Jewish commitment and Jewish involvement. We have made significant
improvements to our building, equipment, programs, services and staff. We have
created a “hamisha” neighborhood, serving people of all ages — from 6 week old
babies to senior adults.
The mission of the JCA is to (1) contribute to the continuation of Jewish life,
culture, and community, (2) provide a common meeting ground for the Jewish
community, (3) enhance the quality of life for all segments of the community, and (4)
strengthen family life. The JCA fulfills its mission through an integrated range of
high quality programs for people of all ages including: child care and family programs;
fitness and recreational facilities and activities; Jewish education, culture and arts
programs; and by providing a place for family, “neighborhood,” and community
gatherings.
It is with great pride that we are able to work with the Jacksonville Jewish
Center and other Jacksonville synagogues and agencies in conducting special
educational programs and holiday celebrations. The JCA serves the Jewish community
by the free use of JCA facilities for all synagogues, the Federation, and other Jewish
organizations.
We have made changes and are continuing to make changes to better serve the
Jewish community and enhance the quality of life. A sliding fee scale is available to make
membership affordable to all. The doors are always open in our neighborhood - please
come in and join our JCA family - Shalom!
River Garden Auxiliary
“Honor thy Father and thy Mother” — this is the ongoing commitment
of the River Garden Auxiliary since it’s beginning in 1922 as the Ladies
Hebrew Sheltering Aid Society. Together with a combination of love,
dedication and hard work, our goal is to help enhance the lives of the residents
of River Garden Hebrew Home.
In order to accomplish our goal, we need the help of each and every
member of the Auxiliary. We also need many new members, not only to
support us financially, but also to find more willing hands to come and share
some of their time with the residents. More and more, younger generations
have come to realize that in our elders we have a precious and useful asset.
Our aim is to make their lives a good deal richer and happier, and in return to
receive the rewards of caring. Our “Helping Hands” make a real difference.
— Gayle D. Bailys, Auxiliary President

===== PAGE 196 =====
support; I always benefited from her
perspective and good sense as to the
things that were important and to
those concerns which I needed to
keep foremost on my mind. I know
that her poise and her charm, her
warmth and dignity have added
immeasurably to whatever success
I have achieved.
Inge and I had the privilege of
being bom into families that provided
us with life’s most precious and
sacred experiences. Our families
lived and breathed Jewish life. Being
a rabbi was really an extension of
my upbringing and my personality
and an expression of my love affair
with things Jewish. Our way in the
world has been gladdened by the
companionship of family and friends.
We are grateful for the joy and
understanding, the naches and
pleasure that our children Asher &
Sabrina, Shalva & David and our
grandchildren Jordana, Yoav Ezra &
Shira have brought us.
The Jewish community lives on
the frontier of a constantly changing
world, facing problems and
challenges that seem unprecedented.
We are concerned about a
weakening of those Jewish ideals
and standards to which former
generations were loyal. We have,
seemingly, paid a high price for our
integration in a free society. The
transmission of tradition from one
generation to the next, is no longer a
given. Some of our religious
traditions are regarded with the
skepticism resulting in a consequent
lessening of the values we have held
most dear. But, as we face the
future, we are confident that this
congregation will be equal to the task
that lies ahead; that our synagogue
will continue to provide a sense of
kedusha — a sacredness which
affirms the enduring meaning of
human existence and Jewish life.
A Jew was defined by Yehuda
Ha-Levi, a medieval and distinguished
poet and philosopher as a “prisoner
of hope”. Because we are prisoners
of hope we believe that the legacy
bequeathed to us over these last
some 100 years of our congregation
will be renewed for the generations
of the future. The American
synagogue has conveyed the
meaning of Jewish existence to the
largest Jewish community that has
ever lived in a free society. We
believe that the Jacksonville Jewish
Center can expand on the best of
our past as it inspires its sons and
daughters to Jewish idealism and
faithfulness in the future. We are
“prisoners of hope”. In the midst of
freedom and security we can
reaffirm our witness to God’s
presence and to our faith in Torah.
Let the record of the Jacksonville
Jewish Center fortify us with the
strength and determination to fulfill
this task for the decades ahead
AMEN.
— Rabbi David Gaffney

Scouting
Junior Girl Scout Troop 5 Cadette Girl Scout Troop 969
Junior Troop 5 expanded to 32 girls this year as the
message got out — Girl Scouting is great!
The troop’s first goal for the year was to earn the “Sign
of the World” which included exploring our community. We
toured the south bank of the river walk, learned about the folk
history of Treaty Oak, watched the Dietary and Sports
Medicine depts. in action and saw how our hearts and lungs
function at the Heart and Lung Gallery at St. Vincent’s Medical
Center, toured Friendship Park, learned about manatees at
MOSH, saw robotics in production at Sally Industries, sat in
on a city council meeting and shared our knowledge with
younger troops.
Our second goal, to earn the “Sign of the Sun” included
fitness and outdoor cooking. We cooked pancakes on camp
stoves at Blue Spring State Park while visiting manatees,
grilled hotdogs on stick at the Gazebo, baked pinwheels in
box ovens and loved the pudding in bags at Camp Kateri. Our
5th and 6th graders at Kateri participated in Aquatics weekend
and learned to sail or wind surf.
To give back to the community we helped replenish the
food cupboard at JFCS, brought baby items to Emergency
Pregnancy Services, cleaned like magic and baked brownies
for families at Ronald McDonald House and held several
events for Brownie and Daisy girl scouts a Travel Conference,
Bicycle Safety Poster Contest, and Fitness is Fun Olympics.
The Cadette Girls Scouts had a great second year at the
Center. They braved the cold winter during a backpacking
trip to Providence Canyon State Park in Georgia, where they
earned their Geology interest patch, camped, cooked outdoors
and made new friendships with other girls from the Gateway
Council Cadette and Senior troops. They also completed, as a
troop, the Conflict Resolution interest patch. The highlight
was the mock court held by the girls with the able assistance
of Jeffery Morris. This may become an annual event if Jeff
is willing!
As another step toward the Silver Award — the second
highest given in Girls Scouting — the troop earned the Cadet
Challenge, an in-depth look at values, community spirit and
relationships. Two Caddettes will complete their Silver Award
this fall, and bridge to the next level, Senior Girls Scouts. The
entire troop will then be a Cadette-Senior troop, as we continue
to build interest at these age levels. We are also excited to
welcome in nine 7th graders from Junior Troop 5!
Many thanks to Robin Morris for her perseverance in
working with the girls on the Menorah Award, the religion
award for Jewish Cadets. We all had fun through the process
with Robin’s support. Thanks again to the Cookie Mom, Cathy
Cohen, for her organization and record-keeping throughout
the cookie sale, and to those who supported the troop with
their purchases.
Three of our 6th graders interviewed and were selected
for Gateway Council’s 6th grade event based on historic St.
Augustine in the 1740’s. Robyn Blum, Emma Lipsky and
Debbie Shacter helped sew and embroider authentic outfits
and camped and served as tour guides in the historic district.
They taught tourists and other Girl Scouts how meals were
prepared outdoors in iron pots over open fires, how candies
were dipped, baskets were woven, games were played,
metalwork was done and more. This is considered a “wider
opportunity” that prepares girls for broader adventures in Girl
Scouting nationally and internationally! We are proud of all
nine sixth graders who bridged up to Cadettes, the next age
level in Girl Scouting.
Thanks to Helen Shacter, who again served as Cookie
Mom, and Shirley Jernigan, always there when needed. Helen
and Shirley will co-lead Troop 5 in 1998-99. Thanks also to
Jill Tager, Badge Mom for keeping our records straight, and
to all the parents for their wonderful support of their daughters
and Troop 5!
For information on the Cadette-Senior levels of Girl
Scouting at the Jacksonville Jewish Center, contact co-leaders
Karen Southall, 292-0843, or Jan Lipsky, 268-7225.
A weekend of backpacking and camping for Cadette Troop 969 at
Providence State, GA, in February 1998.

ADULT EDUCATION
Early in the 1970s, the Adult Study Committee was formed under the guidance of
Rabbi Gaffney to present a variety of programs of special interest to the members of
tiie congregation. It has been expanded and refined over the years and now boasts a
large curriculum of adult studies taught by professionals and knowledgeable laity, a
lecture series that features prominent national and international speakers, an annual
scholar-in-residence weekend, as well as award-winning programs that focus on single
themes or target specific groups.
• SHABBATON
One of the most comprehensive programs developed by Rabbi Gaffney and the Adult
Study Committee was the Shabbaton. It is a weekend designed to totally immerse the
congregation in Jewish thought, stimulated by a highly acclaimed lecturer or
professional educator. Over the years there have been a host of wonderful speakers,
such as, Rabbi Joseph Teluskin, Dennis Prager, Rabbi Joel Roth, Professor Dr. Deborah
Lipstadt, Rabbi David Wolpe, Dr. Irving Greenberg, and storyteller Penina Schram, to
name a few. The newly established Marilyn & Louis Safer Shabbaton Fund perpetually
underwrites this program, assuring that Shabbatons will continue, year after year in
ever increasing popularity.
• SETZER-LEVIT MEMORIAL LECTURE
The Setzer-Levit Memorial Lecture Series has endeavored to raise the consciousness
of the Jewish community by bringing the highest caliber speakers for a single lecture
on important Jewish concerns. Beginning in 1985 with noted author, scholar and lecturer
Rabbi Harold Schulweis, Rabbi Gaffney has been responsible for attracting such fine
speakers as Wolf Blitzer, Senator Joseph Lieberman, Rabbi Avi Weiss, Congressman
Stephen Solarz and Malcolm Hoenlein.
• SISTERHOOD BAT MITZVAH CLASS
These classes were designed and taught by Rabbi Gaffney to offer to adults, regardless
of whether or not they had already celebrated a Bat Mitzvah, a basic Jewish education
covering holidays, the prayer book, Shabbat, kashrut, life cycle events history and
Jewish philosophy.. The culmination of this two year program is an inspiring ceremony
in which the students participate in services throughout Shabbat services, leading
prayers, reading Torah, chanting haftorah and have given sermons. The first class
celebrated their simcha in 1979. Since then 150 women have become Bat Mitzvah, and
the program has expanded to include men.
“For me, growing up in New York, Judaism was more of a group identification,
not a religion you practiced. As a student in one of the Sisterhood's Adult B’nai
Mitzvah classes, Rabbi Gaffney gave me the formal education I never had as a child.
I also enjoyed the class because I got to know the Rabbi on a different level. Rabbi
Gaffney is a wonderful teacher— Bonnie Sandler
• SISTERHOOD SEMINARS
Another program that has stood the test of time is the Sisterhood Seminar. Beginning
in 1979, Rabbi Gaffney met one morning a month, in an informal setting to study topics
of particular interest to women. Last year, “Women in the Bible” promoted lively and
interesting discussions.
"I have always enjoyed the camaraderie of the Sisterhood Seminars, and I appreciate
Rabbi Gaffney giving us his time and sharing his knowledge with us. ” — Joan Waitz
• NEW AMERICAN B’NAI MITZVAH:
The Center Men’s Club introduced this program of intensive Jewish education, with
curriculum outlined by Rabbi Gaffney, and taught by lay leaders of our congregation.
It was a rewarding experience for both students and teachers and earned the Golden
Torch Award, the highest honor given to programs by the Federation of Jewish Men’s
Clubs.
“He [Rabbi Gaffney] made a great impact on our lives. He turned complete
atheists, which we were when we came to America, into real Jews. He has always
been there for us: first by teaching us for the B’nai Mitzvah, and then by making my
daughter Vicky’s Bat Mitzvah very special, and my other daughter Galina’s wedding
outstanding! ” — Svetlana Goldiner

Recreation
Center Day Camp — The Place to Be!
Center Day Camp programs were hopping this summer! In addition to the regular
fun camp activities like swimming, arts and crafts, and Judaica, our campers watched a
Jaguar practice and were able to get autographs. They went bowling; played laser tag and
putt-putt golf; went to Wet ‘N Wild; and to a movie. Officer Friendly visited. Campers
had a great time on the “moonwalk” and ate at Semolina’s, where they made pasta. They
had a carnival with fun booths; went tubin’ down the Itchitucknee; and spent some great
nights at “lock-ins.”
Our Preschool campers did fun activities with cats, rabbits, bears, dinosaurs and
forest animals. Another fun theme was planes, trains and automobiles. There were mornings
filled with cooking, reading, singing and pretending.
Speciality Camps were a hit with everyone.
Cheerleading Campers not only cheered, jumped and
danced, but made great outfits to wear, as well. They
are ready for the “roar!”
Drama Campers focused on Disney. They were
“on stage” for five entertaining “productions” from
Aladdin, Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs, Mary
Poppins, and Lion King. Their costumes were hand
made by Gayle Bailys.
Golf Campers visited the World Golf Village
in St. Augustine and played nine holes at Palm Valley.
PGA here we come!
Basketball and Baseball Camps were loads of fun with days spent playing ball,
sharpening skills and making friends.
Mitzvah Campers spent two days at Angel Aid, where they helped make “bottles of
love” to be sold as one of their fundraisers. These bottles contained recycled and shredded
birthday and anniversary cards. “Angel escapes,” sand and seashells in clear plastic balls,
were made for sick children to look at just prior to surgery. Campers also went on a kosher
food hunt, and collected food for FANN.
In Arts and Crafts Camp, they made
some outstanding items, including edible ones. They dipped pretzels in chocolate
and drizzled chocolate on popcorn. They also made beaded gecko and bug key
chains, a fimo shabbat set and hot plates using mosaic tiles.
Sports campers did anything with a ball and had a ball doing it! Their
activities included baseball, basketball, flag football, hockey and bombardment.
Our camp counselors were outstanding, our CITS were great, and our campers
were the best! Thank you Gayle Bailys, Ellen Balotin, Carol Goldberg, Manya
Osher, Edith Horovitz, Sharon Seebol, Shirley Jernigan, Hana Bendit and the
great pool staff.

===== PAGE 225 =====
Center Youth Groups
Chalutzim - Grades 4 and 5
Research has proven that the survival of Judaism depends on the exposure of our youth to
Jewish activities, friends and experiences that commit them to perpetuating that feeling of
Jewishness and Jewish life.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center sponsors three outstanding youth groups for youngsters in
grades 4-12. Each group meets regularly and enjoys programs of a religious, cultural and social
nature.
Through active participation in these groups, a sense of pride and an identification with
Judaism are instilled. Jewish values, attitude and behavior patterns are discussed and carried out
through Mitzvah programs and study.
Conventions, regional activities and camps give our youth the opportunity to meet other
Jewish youth from all over the United States.
The youth programs are coordinated by Rabbi Dov Kentof, and are supervised
by the Youth Commission. All groups are affiliated with the Southeast Region and
United Synagogue of America.
— 1998-99

===== PAGE 234 =====
Committees
Adult Education
Expanding one’s knowledge in Judaism is more
important than almost any other of the 613 commandments.
To answer the diverse educational needs of our congregation,
the Adult Education Committee coordinated an ambitious
program with a wide variety of courses and speakers
throughout the year. Hebrew literacy, Talmud, synagogue and
holiday workshops, Family University, Firing Line and other
discussion groups formed the basis of a comprehensive, on¬
going curriculum. The Setzer-Levit Memorial Lecture,
Shabbaton and community-based engagements brought
prominent speakers of national and international acclaim.
Exciting plans to enrich your spiritual life in the coming year
are underway.
The Adult Education Committee, with Professor Shalom Paul.
Our lecture calendar began at Selichot with Washington Post diplomatic reporter, Michael
Dobbs, who had just broken the story to the world of Secretary of State Madeleine Albright’s
Jewish roots and her tragic family history. Mr. Dobbs shared his experiences in the company
of Mrs. Albright while visiting Czechoslovakia.
Shabbaton Weekend, underwritten by the Marilyn and Louis
—¿ÉlP^Jji Safer Shabbaton Fund, featured the entertaining and popular
JÜ speaker, Professor Shalom Paul, chairman of the Bible department
Michael Dobbs at Hebrew University. Regarded as one of the most noted scholars in
the world today, Professor Paul brought the Creation to life with all
the animation, drama and humor of a theatrical performance. The congregation was
educated and uplifted throughout this most enjoyable weekend.
Stuart Schoffman, Associate Editor and cultural Professor Shalom Paul
columnist of the international bi-weekly magazine, The
Jerusalem Report, addressed the issues of “Israel at 50” in two sessions presented by
the Setzer-Levit Memorial Lecture. Mr. Schoffman provided glimpses of the promises
and challenges that face Israel, from an insider’s perspective.
Several times throughout the year, the Firing Line
program provides forums for exploring contemporary Jewish
Stuart Scoffman issues using current periodicals as motivators for discussion.
One session, however, featured a speaker, Dr. Ralph
Lowenstein, Dean Emeritus of College of Jerusalem at the University of Florida. He
discussed the military role Americans played in the war for Israeli independence and
the ramifications of this involvement 50 years later.
During Seminary Shabbat, Eytan Hammerman, a student at the Jewish Dr. Ralph Lowenstein
Theological Seminary, gave us his reflections on the preparation he is receiving as a
future leader in the Conservative Movement. Family University, directed by Pam Maman, offered parents
and students of the Solomon Schechter Day School a unique opportunity to attend classes chosen from a wide
range of topics taught by knowlegeable members of our community.

Religious Schools
Sunday School
The SUNDAY SCHOOL of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is
planned expressly for children in kindergarten, first and second grades. A
weekly, two-hour program gives each child the opportunity to experience
the richness of his/her Jewish heritage through song, dance, role playing,
cooking, short stories, games, arts and crafts. Emphasis is placed on the
holidays and festivals. Jewish values and mitzvot are encouraged. Many
thanks to our wonderful Sunday School teachers Susan Kadish, Sharona
Kadish and Susan Neadle.
Students included Daniel Abramson, Sarah Abramson, Lillian
Anderson, David Cantlon, Jeremy Cantlon, Alyssa DeCrispino,
Jordan Kress, Danielle Lewis, Alyssa Libón, Melissa Neadle, Jacob
Factor, Danielle Palombo, Benjamin Peltz, Joshua Peretzman, Mark
Safer, Harrison Safer, Paul Sandler, Molly Seebol, Stephanie Seebol,
Shlomo Shemesh, Emily Talpalar, Abigail Weiss and Scott Youker.
Family Council
At right:Mrs. Debbie Banks, Tot Shabbat
coordinator, with one of her young congregants.
Pre-Junior Congregation
Kindergarten-2nd Grade
Meets Saturdays, lla.m.-Noon
Below: Pre-Junior Congregation participants.
For ten years, FAMILY COUNCIL has
provided innovative Family Education programs
involving all facets of the congregation. Several
large scale projects like Rabbi Dov Kentof’s
Fantasy Voyage on Noah’s Ark to the Zoo, Sukkah
Decorating and Hanukkah Activity Day inspire the
entire congregation including the Center
Preschool, Solomon Schechter Day School,
Afternoon Hebrew School and Sunday School.
Synagogue professionals, volunteer experts,
parents and children provide valuable input and
assistance and are rewarded by the experience.

Warmest congratulations to Rabbi David
Gaffney on the celebration of 25 years at the
Jacksonville Jewish Center. As the spiritual
leader of our congregation, you have profoundly
influenced the lives of our Sisterhood members.
You have been a guiding force in the continuing
education of women in our congregation.
Through the Sisterhood Bat Mitzvah program
and monthly Sisterhood Semináis, which you
developed and continue to implement* women in
our congregation are growing in all aspects of
Jewish life. You have been sensitive to our needs
as women, as well as to our changing role in the
Conservative movement, and with your
encouragement we are taking an even more active
part in synagogue life. We thank you and wish
you Mazal tov!
Jacksonville Jewish Center

Religious Schools
Afternoon Hebrew School
The Afternoon Hebrew School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is designed for students in grades 3-7, and provides an
elementary education leading to Bar/Bat Mitzvah and continuation in the high school program.
Meeting on Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays, “the basics” are at the core of the curriculum, with stress on Hebrew
reading, Jewish social studies, and current events relating to Israel. Synagogue skills, holiday observances and knowledge of
prayers are all part of the comprehensive Afternoon Hebrew School program.
Aleph Class: Teachers - Carole Goldberg, Alina Kentof
Students: Michael Cantlon, Leah Dubin, Kari Ginsberg, Michelle
Jernigan, Ali Margolies, Joshua Marks, Andrew Schemer,
Michelle Spivak, Brittany Vitiello, Tess Wilensky.
Bet Class: Teachers - Carole Goldberg, Pamela Maman, Nili
Grinberg. Students: Julie Fixel, Erika Goodfarb, Chloe Hochrad, Megan
Libón, Ashley Osterer, SaraPeretzman, Risa Portnoy, Stephanie Shacter,
Jonathan Shriftman, Jamie Talpalar, Melissa Wyzan.
Cathy Wilensky and Ava Axelrod
PTA Presidents
Supplemental School PTA
We are looking forward to another exciting year with our Afternoon Hebrew,
Sunday School and Beit Midrásh classes.
Our younger students seem to become more involved each year with our Jewish
Holidays. They love the programs they can put on for Passover and Purim. Our older
students are becoming serious, committed Jews.
Parental involvement is so very important in a child’s religious education.
Volunteers are always needed, and I believe your children benefit from seeing you
helping out. Please feel free to volunteer whenever you are able, showing your support for
our programs.
Wishing you a wonderful and healthy New Year!
— Cathy and Ava
